et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	and if the artery is large, then it is necessary that you tie it with two threads of strong silk thread, which can withstand the pressure before the wound, and withstand the flow of blood;
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	Then remove the excess which is between the two lips in that same hour, and then, if you see, if the cauterization of the cautery is next to the bone as long as the head is removed;
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and it's a work for the doctor, if the patient has no fever and he is of a warm temperament.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For cauterizations are helped in ending the illnesses:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	because it is of greater aid to the illnesses.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Where it is necessary for the extraction of the arteries that one fills the body with old cotton and puts it on well-made tents;
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when one unwinds them, let them be cured with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with tents, until they are healthy;
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and without cutting the artery as long as you have work to do, if you are in a hurry to cure by cauterization, or you fill the body with vitriol and squeeze with your hand so that the blood is congealed;
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you have not that present, then put your finger on the place so long as the blood is congealed, and raise the limb from cold water as soon as the blood stops, and hold it steady as is necessary;
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	and that which is more painful and less gentle in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting on two sides, but the cutting be well spaced to withstand longer their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the extremities are too thin, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And there should be between the two cuts a thumb of thickness, and then when you have signed to put the two limbs together, and you put the iron burning on until it comes near the bone, and cut the vein in two places;
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and be separated between the two parts for it is not suitable to be joined by this cautery in every respect;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and it is the form of the cauterization:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are on the outer skin of the head, and it does not benefit from any medical treatment that one makes, and you see the face of the patient become inflamed, and feel on the forehead a numbness as if from shivering;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and if the eyes are tender and moist so that the hair of the papers is stained, and the papers are scorched, and burned by the heat of the tears, then there is need for this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "confused cure", and it is that you make for the patient who has this disease the hairs that he has on the forehead, then make three equal incisions on the forehead according to the length of the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and let one of the incisions be thus, two fingers deep in the forehead going downwards to the nail, and the other two on either side of the papers, and beware of the incision of the arteries that are on either side of the papers;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and stretch out your hand from the continuation of the two jawbones, and let each wound be the quantity of three fingers across the joints;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and bind many rags around it to absorb the blood, then cut the spatula sharp from two parts where there is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	of the incision that is above the temple just to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape out all the core that is between the two fissures to the entire surface which is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision just to the other second, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you cut in the first fissure the instrument that is called "cultellaire", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is soft, not cutting, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the cauterized part cutting towards the flesh near the heart, and let the cauterized part soften towards the bone, and let it thicken until it reaches the middle fissure.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut off the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as long as the incision is continuous up to what opens from the heart, and then make another cut in the middle fissure up to the other side;
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then extract equally from the blood, and press the limb for the blood taken;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put on draped moistened with wine and oil and vinegar, and guard that abscesses do not come;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day untie the linen, and apply a great plaster of hot water, then the treatment of unction with basilicon oil, and other treatments that one cures wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	Two humors of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When in any corner there is an acute and customary cataract, and you see the eyes thin and small, and the sight weakened, and the pupils burned;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and the head is deeply painful, and the patient is in agony;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then it is known by these accidents that these matters and this catharr do not come from many veins, and the doctor knows what the cure is, if it exists.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to shave his forehead, then make a great incision in the forehead, and another of two fingers in width.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And let the incision be from the left temple to the right temple, and it shall be just to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and dislodge your hand from the nerves of the temples that move to the brain;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood with a sponge, and then swab between the two lips of the wound and put in a lot of cotton, and bandages of linen;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then apply warm dressings moistened with wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is inflamed, it is necessary that you rub the bone as long as the flesh begins to grow, then treat it with caustic things, which cause flesh to grow.
En teil maniere:	In a similar manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take two parts of flower of centaury, and four parts of celandine, and make a plaster;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer it to these wounds to cause flesh to grow throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that falls into the ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	Oats, or beast, or stone of mine or similar things as iron.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seeds, like jasper, beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing things such as aqua and urine and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When there is a stone in the ear or another kind of thing that does not belong to the ear, nor grows in the ear, then put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, apply a poultice of violet oil or oil of cypress, then attempt extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and make him sneeze with a concoction, and stop up his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool in the ear;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and press the ear downward.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times a discharge comes out through this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come out by itself, then one must perform a subtle extraction with careful pinchings, from which this is the method:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it comes out by itself through the pinchings, that's good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, then one must perform an extraction with a subtle hook of small doubled thread;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not come out through that, then make a thread of silk and push the head of the thread through the hole of the ear strongly, and stuff that which is around the thread with wax so that the veins cannot enter with the thread;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then pull it out strongly, for many times it comes out as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come out in that manner, then take glue of this kind and take the arteries, and put some instrument which has a point for doing that, and put a little cotton around;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the flesh against the stone or whatever it is, and pull strongly.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not come out from all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear as well as the abscess is hot and swollen, and spasms;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of the cutting is that you first let blood from the patient's head, and extract blood according to the measure of its virtue, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut in the root of the ear at the fat or dependent flesh;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the cut be as wide as a reed, until you reach the stone, then extract the bone according to your power, and suck it hastily with your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the treatment until he is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it's a grain that is embedded and has swollen, then administer extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot exit, then apply the spatula needle subtly according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do it when you think that the grain is moistened by the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract it with subtle pinchers and a sucker, as we have said, so that the extraction is alleviated.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case then that there is a discharge in the ear, it is necessary for the patient to use a remedy of condiments first, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it rest on the same ear where the discharge is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If blood comes out because of that, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If this is not so, then take many stones according to the length of your hand and fingers and toes, and heat them a little by fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and put them in the patient's ear or through his ears, and rub on the soles of his feet on the other side, and make friction with another foot on the foot that is by the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not stop rubbing foot against foot until the fever has entirely gone, and thus the fever will be entirely gone;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see, then take a reed, and thrust one end into the ear, and the other end is pressed against fire until the hottest part of the reed is burned;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then do another piece of the reeds in the same way until the fever is entirely gone, as we have said before.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of a beast, if it is small in body, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the section;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of large size so that one can feel it, then administer the extraction of splinters;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and it is the lightest thing to remove what is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the removal of worms from the ears, when you perform the cure as we have said in the section and treatise on distillations, and the cure is not beneficial, then it is necessary to examine the ear in sunlight:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if there are no visible worms, then treat them as subtle splinters, and if they are not visible, take the chain from which this form is made:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow at the top and wide at the bottom.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And insert the thinnest end into the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then suck firmly on the chain;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, then stuff cotton into the cavity as I have said in the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not come out readily as we have said, then administer distillations that the old ones have experienced in the treatment of worms, and you will find them or the treatment of distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you administer your oils and medicines in the ear with all this equipment, according to its form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And be it of silver or of brass, make strainers for the small openings, and above them put sieves to administer drops;
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press inside the distillation the instrument of brass made for this purpose, and if you see the discharge and envelop it with cotton around the pointed end;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then put your oil or your juice, and that which you see of your medicines in the cavity, and let the cane be in the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	Then thrust your finger inside the nostril of the entire coty, and press your hand temporarily as long as the oil is distilled or removed from the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and let the patient feel inside, and let the distillations be warmed by the fire, just as one distills in the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppage of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born who does not have a passage in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and this same thing happens to men through stoppage of a wound, or of a flesh born inside the ear, and these stoppings come sometimes deep into the ear, so that one cannot see it;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes it happens that the passage is blocked, and one sees it very well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which comes from the depths, if one cannot see it, is of grievous sanitation in many conditions, and in this one sees that you must put the patient's ear to the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look within:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the opilation apparent, if the work has all this spatula of which is its form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let it be sharp and cutting at the front and back entirely flat, so that it does not touch the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the opilation is of flesh near or on the ear, if you hold it with subtle pinces, and cut it lightly, until that flesh is all removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the opilation is deep in the ear, take a subtle rasp lightly and heat it a little by the fire, then put it on the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you suspect an obstruction where the patient feels pain in the ear, perforate lightly, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then put in the ear a tent made from the width of the perforation, and the stopper in Egyptian application.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this on no day until the wound is healed, or take a tent and stopper made from rose water, and powder with burnt vitriol;
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear inflamed, it is necessary that you pull out the tent and put in another moistened one made from wax which is made of rose oil and wax, until the inflammation is reduced;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat him until he is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if discharge of blood comes, dip a sponge in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that reduce the discharge of blood which are found in the treatises on distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	It is useful for the eyes when they come in papers of the eyes when they are moist and dry, it is necessary that you extend them with tongs and pincers, and the head of a spatula of its roots;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put on the limb vitriol ointment.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And without removing it, if the cauterization of a subtle lenticular cauterizer is good, and the cauterizer after the incision is worth more;
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and many times repair, when anything remains from their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, then are burned those roots and do not regrow again.
de la gresle	of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come in papers of the eyes things that seem gravel in shape and hardness, and for this reason is this disease called "gravel", and it is a gathering of thick moisture in the paper of above and below;
li ovraiges est telz:	The works are such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	it is obvious that the swelling decreases on one side and the other, and it is an easy thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	make a poultice of dough then lightly scrape off the roughness from each part, then take it with pinchers and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	if you cannot cut it without piercing a little of the skin, do not grievously harm the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the fissure is large, then assemble it with a suture, and treat it until it is healed;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not apply any pressure, for the organs will restore it at once and join with flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the swelling descends inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn the skin, and stretch the swelling with pinchers, and cut and press it from one side and the other;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the plaster is removed by cutting, it does not cause any harm;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the stone is cut, if you lift the eyelid of the salty eye, and treat the place that is full of stones until the patient is healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a fat that is formed in the corners of the eyelids, and this happens more to children than to old people, and it causes them much trouble with their eyes, and they get catarrh in the morning, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and because of this they often lie on their faces, and sleep on them, and their eyelids become moist under their eyebrows, which the discharge and appearance of the exinach that appears in the eye have covered.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb with your fingers and feel the hernia between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts their head in your hands;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a bandage in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains the hernia on each part, then put it on them;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the hernia is gathered together within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make in the middle of the moisture a incision with a sharp scalpel, one finger wide, and not wider than the wound one makes on the vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and make the skin deep enough that you come to the hernia;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in many cases the hernia comes out of the incision, in the shape of a piece of white fatty tissue.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Remove then a piece of torn cloth from your fingers at the end, and turn your hand to the right and to the left as far as it is separated;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and beware that you do not put in the fissure, that you do not approach the whole spatula to the eye, that you do not touch it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the suture does not appear at the beginning of the fissure, then increase a little the fissure lightly until it appears;
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then remove it as we have said, then moisten cloths in vinegar and in water, and put on the wound, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if it is one of those men who break the seal and put on to corrupt that moisture which has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat him until he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes to the wound, then cure it with soothing plasters until it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	The hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When in the papers hairs grow joined with other than their nature, and are inflamed, if they harm the eyes, and bring forth manners of sickness such as customary tears and softening of the papers and albuge, so that it is a cause of destruction of the eyes;
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and the treatment is according to four methods:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	by fire cauterization together with heat, or by sharp medicine according to that which is said in the chapter of cauterization, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by burns, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you put the head of the sick person on your right shoulder, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If it is converted, it is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then insert a needle to the entire thread beneath;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let it be that the margin of the parchment where the hairs grow among these hairs, and pull the thread to the top across all the parchment, and turn it to the scraper;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make on the part under the parchment, under the hairs joined, to all the spatula scraping, from the large scissor to the small;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then extract the thread, and put under the parchment a small piece of cotton and of cloth, then draw on the parchment a figure of ink, such as the shape of a witness, and however it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see elevated the parchment which is divided into pieces.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if a part of the trade where one cuts a large quantity of parchment according to that which the parchment is softened;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then make on all the spatula along the two lines that you have drawn, and begin with the large scissor to the small;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let it be one of the fissures near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the onion in one of the two angles of the heart, then scratch everything;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then assemble the two lips with a stitch of a needle to all the subtle thread of wool, and suck the blood, and make dry the superfluity of threads on the two eyebrows with any glutinous things, if you want to do this;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, then I have no cure, then leave the stitch and the threads until three or four days;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then cure the wound without stitching of dry and constricting things, for the skin relives at the suddenness of the wound and the assembling of it, but the stitch is bad (as the ancients said), and it is work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere:	and if in another manner:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you show the sheet of a figure which is as the liver of the spleen, as we have described, to three ounces of powder according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut that which overcomes the small equal forces according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you do not have the power to hold the clamps, and the thing is not equal, take a needle or thread, and put it in the middle of the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and put another thread through the large arm, and the second thread through the small one, and join between your two hands the threads equally;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin upon which you have signed, as we have described, then join the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to a cutting, thus one calms the patient with similar soothing ointments;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes it happens that the hair of the nipple are converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	if it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitching on one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of pains is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and it is that you turn the nipple and the skin within according to what I have said, and then make two pains by art, and two subtle threads as long as the nipple and the width of the spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut at the two heads of the two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble one and the other subtly on what protrudes from the nipple of the eye, and pull the two pains of the two parts forcibly;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and let it be so for some days, and the skin that is constricted will die and putrefy and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it delays, if the scab forms a strong layer, then let the scab form until it is healthy;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound has been sucked, and if the skin is lifted, and no longer will the hairs prick;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and it is the shape of the two canthi that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width;
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the work is such that you take a fine needle, and put in it a thread of soft and fine silk;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then assemble the heads and tie one and the other finely, and let the length of the threads be a palm of length;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then arrange in the flesh another fine thread of silk quickly, and tie the head of the two threads;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then put the patient's head in your hands;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let it be beneath the sun so that your work may be declared, for this is a subtle and minor work, then stick the needle to the entire lock at the root of the hair adjacent to it, and make it pierce the skin hastily as long as you draw it out from above the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then pull out the hair up to the lock, and stick into the lock that hair, if there is one or two or three or several;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then pull out your hand so that the hairs come out entirely from the lock in the skin with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the lock is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the lock downward with all the thread that you had prepared, until the lock comes out from the skin and you see it through the vision of the eye;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then if you treat the wound and the thread, and close the eye and let it close for two or three days, until the hair adheres to its place and the flesh grows over it;
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hairs are small, then accompany the small hair with the natural long hair of the eyebrows, and let it be joined with that which you left, until it is lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the corruption of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease called "alexati" or corruption comes into the eye, it is in two manners:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one is natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it comes from a sudden blow, or from a cut, or from cauterization, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of the work in it is that you split the suture, and separate the lips of it, and put inside tendons of linen, and lift them until they are healed;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not necessary that you use in the treatment of those things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do that, the illness returns worse than the first one;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but to apply things that soften, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the roots of a plant or tree and seeds of flax be cooked, and anointments of dyachylon melted in some oil, and it wrapped in a bandage, and the treatment of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasures of your treatment are that you take care that it not become sour according to the form it had before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these works that we have said are not outside of remedies for this illness, that it does not return according to the form it had before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is disordered is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accidental comes from a wound and from a fissure and from cauterization and from similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the way of the work in this case is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and the stitch in the flesh, and you make it pierce from the left arm to the right, so that the threads come out at the two ends of the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then the flesh is sewn over the top of the entire needle, and it is cut with a spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the papier returns according to what is needed, it is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if not, then take a rasp and put it in the fissure, and turn the papier, and make two fissures or cut within the papier;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the head of the two fractures of the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is as the figure of a letter which has no "I griesche
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then sew up that flesh, according to the quantity that its edges are adapted, with that which follows the parchment, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of linen.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with what we have said about softening medicines, and with bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the sickness comes from a fracture or from a surgical incision or from a cauterization, then you should make a flat incision beneath the hairs of the parchment, and according to what is written before;
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then separate between the two lips of a bandage, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare a device for all that they can do to make the shape return to its natural form;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the same patient, according to what work and instrument is needed in various conditions.
dou soudement de la papiere	pain suddenly in the bladder
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this sudden pain has come to men in such a manner that the bladder is seized with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must put the point of a razor under the bladder, and lift it up;
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and you stretch it with pincers, until you cut what is adhering to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot suffer that the too sharp spatula does not injure the eye;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and let your incision be such that you scratch the assembled one lightly, so that the skin regrows according to its natural form;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and it heals the entire assembly, and sometimes forms in the oily bitter sauce, and the sweet water of the liver;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then put between the skin and the oil a thread of flax, and put on the oil wool moistened in abundance of egg;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after the third day, apply sweet liver and hot things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the unction of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	It is known that the unguent is in two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	one is nervous and similar to a hard skin, and another which is not nervous, but is similar to a white moist congelation, which when one touches it with iron and cuts the flesh with pincers, it cannot be felt;
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and one and the other symptom increases towards the large artery, and grows little by little until it covers all the vein and all the light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts his head in a position, then covers his eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and raises the skin with one hand, then takes the needle to the pinches of small doubling, and stretches it to the underside;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then takes a needle, and puts the hair of a horse, or of a cow, or of an ox, and a strong thread;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and doubles the point of the needle a little and puts it in the nail, and pierces it with all the needle, and ties the nail with a thread and stretches it to the underside, and scrapes all the hair the cost of the nail which follows the prune and the thread to the hair just to the head, then cuts the remaining part in the root of the artery with all the spatula subtle and small forces, and lets the natural flesh or artery, so that by the incision does not come the body of the arteries accustomedly;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes the nail adheres to the tendon solely, and to the thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then one scrapes all the spatulum gently from where this is the shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And take care that the spatula does not touch the thin flesh and tear it, and that the needle is not perforated;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision, put in the eye a little of powdered salve, and made from litharge, and let it stay there until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then one cures that which is necessary as long as he is sick.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not numb, and you cannot push the needle, and the nails cannot enter, often this type of nail is cured with medicines;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and grows thus as I have described in the division, and if you see it covered, or the eye of the patient is closed, and take the spatula lightly a little sharp according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And rub the onion gently upwards, and if you see that it diminishes somewhat and the reason presses upon it, then distill from your mouth into the hollow cylinder made of litargire and red collier and broiet, and stop up the oil until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then resume the other work according to this same method, as long as it is all bone.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the oil, as with a hot abscess, then anoint it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healthy, then resume the work as before, until it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh of the arm causes great harm in the oil due to a serious wound, then suck on the wound, and cut off a part but not all, so that no pus comes from the wounds;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill in the red oil collirium which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the flesh that grows on the plum tree
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	It is in the eyes of some men that red flesh grows, and covers the plum and presses on the papers and turns to the defect, and resembles a rose of baluster;
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the work of it is that the patient puts his head in a warm place, then opens the eyes, and takes out all that flesh with sharp scalpels, and supports it with force;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut the first flesh, and continue cutting to the root until the end, and beware that you do not spill the oil on the work;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision of the spatula be as we have said in the incision of the ingle and the small forces that one cuts with the Sebile bone, as the form shows after this chapter where it is demonstrated;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, then apply the oil of distilled broom or you distill red collirium and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the wound cotton with vinegar of rose, so that it is cauterized by hot aposteme;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if it remains nothing, and the blood cold overcomes, and you doubt hot aposteme, then leave the oil and treat the aposteme with things that appease the hot aposteme;
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work as long as it is healthy, and thus do where the flesh is adjusted in the oil by this similarity.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But nevertheless it is necessary that you lift the treatment of each weak oil from the natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and from the accidental way, in work of iron;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from the work.
des voines des eulz	Of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	There are red veins that are hidden under the eye, and take away its function and weaken the eye entirely.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is necessary first that you examine the eye, in which the vein is, if it is outside, and not another disease of the eye besides the vein;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then take the vein in a suitable manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then press those veins all along the shoulder according to your wisdom, and let the shoulders be subtle and double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two shoulders of equal size on the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then press the vein with force subtly, and let the blood come out hour after hour, until you see the veins of the eye move again;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and beware that you do not block the eyes at the points of the spatulas, and perform this work at midday before the sun, and be very careful in your work so that you do not touch the veins except those.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, then distill into the eye a green and red collirium to corrupt what remains of the cataract.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you do not have the power to collect all that in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye with things that ease the pain of the eyes, and let it be for some hours until the pain is eased and the abscess is relieved by heat, then resume according to this method which is described before, until it is healed.
et c’est li forme des forces:	and these are the forms of the fractures:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The physician calls them "arissati" fistulas:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	when you treat them with cauterization and hot burning medicine according to what I previously said, and it is not healed, then a wick is put in the wound where it should drain, and pull out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then remove all the instrument of which this form is made;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called " rough head", and let the iron be made sharp to a pointed end, and let it be pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put on the bone of the corrupted flesh, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you feel that the corruption has been removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this sometimes, then restore the place with medicines that draw out.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the places are swollen, and there is a tumor, and the body of the bowel is swollen, and it remains thus for 40 days, and it does not suppurate and is not abscessed, and no bad accident comes, know that he is healthy;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	if it is not so, then there is another trick for bringing the fistula to the pierced hole of the naval according to this method:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you discover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is discovered, then take the iron according to this method, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the handle be tapered up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then put it on the bone of the arm, and withdraw your hand from the elbow a little, then turn all the iron until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it by that which comes in if he puts his hand on his naval;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the limb with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh becomes numb and hardens the limbs, thus it goes to the matter at the kidney;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the discharge of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are open and the pain is everywhere, and it does not come from disturbing the kidney, nor emaciation, then it is necessary that you read to the patient;
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then apply the ointment, then put leeches or apply heat to cause suction, then apply on the eye a plaster made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then extract the eye, and fill it with bandages and dressings;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the dressings is that you take dressings soft enough, and fold each one in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs;
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	Then strain by means of a hard bandage above, and reapply the ventoses to suck without piercing.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then apply the ventoses and let the oil be strained for a day and night, and if the ulcers become soft, then you must strain them a lot;
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then apply the ointment after the day and night, and if you see the oil repairing, it's good;
se ce non;	If not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reapply the plaster and the dressings and the ointment and the ventoses until he is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of rupture of a torn vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When ruptures come in the torn vein, then it opens, and comes out of the fibers like a grain of resin, and is horrible to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Then if you want to close the wound, the work is such that you put a needle in the root of the affected part just above the skin, then put another needle where it has the double thread of the part of the armier;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then cut the thread of double wire and tie a part of the vein around, and constrain it well, then extract the needle and put on the moist woolen cloth in abundance of vinegar;
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and let it be until the thread adheres with the vein, then treat the wound with comforting things until the wound is healed;
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and often the wound is constrained by the vein enclosing a part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eye has great appearance, thus it is pierced at the subtle spatulum which comes from the depth of the wound, and the moist albugine is scraped and the eye is lowered, and it enters within as much as;
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the cavity of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This illness called "alcunnati" is not outside the cavity that is assembled in the eye, resembling a descending vein, and it is not a vein;
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit upright and straight, then take the head between your hands on both sides, and move it as much as you see the cavity coming out above to your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then let it be fixed, and not descending, and let the light be disordered, and the patient sees things as he usually does;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is a vein, and if the descension of the cavity is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and make it go on the cornial web one drop by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornial web and the cornea, as much as the cavity is;
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is dislocated, if it drips into the warm oil or honey mixture to halfway, or warm poultice is applied and halfway, then let it be treated with another treatment until it is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	of the warmth of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have seen the similarities of the warm things in the division, and that which is necessary to pierce;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if one operates according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and apply to him the healthy oil and bind it very tightly;
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then put the cloth with the oil on your left hand if his eyes are on the left, or on your right hand if his eyes are on the right;
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand, if his eyes are on the left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if his eyes are on the right;
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then put the point of the instrument within the crown by the thickness of a reed in that bladder of the eye to the lower part of the lesser arm, then push the instrument which is called «almagda» gently, and turn your hand as long as it pierces into the bladder of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing;
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and it is necessary that the measurement of the path of almagda be at the depth of the measurement of the space which is from the prunelle just to the end of the blackness;
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and it is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	if you see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the cornial web, and then put the instrument just to where the vein is, then press one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the vein descends now, thus the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After a short rest, and if the pain returns through the second path, put the staff with the instrument, and when it is stuck and does not move, extract it gently turning your hand little by little;
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then put on the pain a bit of gum seed, and apply to that eye from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by virtue on the stopped-up eye a wet linen cloth in rose oil and in abundance of egg, and anoint it with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our kind, put on the common people a broth with an abundance of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the extract cannot enter the eye due to its thickness, because there are some men who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", whose form is this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then pierce the conjunctive moderately, and do not go too deep, but make the subtle incision, then apply the poultice, as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a comfortable bed, where he can sleep on his back in a dark place;
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and let him avoid all movements, and take light foods, and not move his head to the right or left, and let him be laid according to his condition until the third day;
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then untie him in the same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see certain things, and then put him back to bed until the seventh day;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not necessary that you do this during the work of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you alleviate this, because the pain rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	Abscesses of the hand come, that you untie the oil before the seventh hour, and take care of those who have an abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is appeased, untie the vein and put on his face a golden plate to cover any hour, and let him be at that time in the dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then go out of the little house little by little, and change into his clothes;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no disciples should interfere with this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us who was from the Arabic region, who told us that in their country they make a plaster called almagra, which draws out the water, but nonetheless I have never seen any of it in our land, nor have I ever read about it in books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and by chance it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the similarities of the forms of almagra, because those who do not recognize them will see.
et soient d’arain proprement:	and are of Arabian origin properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And they are the head of the subtlety in this same subject, and the third angle is acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the hole above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes there are born or produced in the nose various holes, because of which there are some that appear as scorpions with many feet;
