et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if it has such or if it has a hole with a black color of soot, and if it has a hole of brown color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In this case then of these holes which is brown, and not blackened, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands against the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open its nostrils, and pour the onion on those holes, and rub the three fingers;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Then consider that you must sustain the sharp subtle spatula on one side, as long as you know that the instrument is entirely bony.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if anything remains that you cannot cover, then open it to all the subtle and lightweight instruments, so that nothing remains;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and let it be without being overwhelmed, or if an abscess forms, then drain it as is necessary;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if it is malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize the wound as much as the blood needs to be stanched and all the flesh eaten away, then apply egg whites or vinegar and sharp wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the wound does not open, and pus comes just to the palate, know that it is healthy;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if pus does not come through as is necessary, know that there is a new flesh in the bone above, for which the instruments do not need to be sharpened;
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Then it is necessary that you put a thread of flax, somewhat thick, and let it be known by us, and have between each knot a space of one finger or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient's head down to the thread in his nose so he can feel it, and pull it in drawing out as long as it comes through the nose into the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times this is shown to the child at school, and it's an easy thing for one who wants to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the end which comes through the nose in one hand, and the other end which comes through the mouth in the other hand, and pull one after the other being careful as we are with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted that flesh, then pull out the threads, suck the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Make this for three days or more, as long as the ulcers consume all that remains of flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put on a plaster of pounded roots for some days until it is healthy, and if there is need for dry medications, then use them;
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, through which one distills the oils and the medications;
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And let it be of silver or of copper, similar to a covered lamp, like a chain, and the conductor thus;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see fit, make a closed chain, and let the instruments be flat to purge the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have a handle at the top to hold it when one warms up the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease occurs on the head near the nose which is called "telul", and grows and becomes large, so that it is a visible thing to look at;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this reason it is necessary that you cut at the beginning, and remove all dead tissue, then apply the cauterization or the burning medicine;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and let it be covered until it becomes large, if it is hard, of dark color, with little sensation;
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if you do not touch it with iron, for that is an incised abscess, because when one cuts into it, great evil comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of dark color, and you see that it can all be covered, then warn the patient and cut with caution, and treat the wound with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Be aware that when a solution of continuity occurs in one of these cartilaginous operations, it profits little, except for some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is necessary then when it happens to anyone, if one examines whether the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then adjusts the two lips of a wound to a suture, then cures it until it is healed;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are separated from one side to another, then it is necessary that you cauterize all the parts of the wound until they heal, then assemble the two lips in a suture, and strain it, and powder with powdered blood of dragon, and burnt incense;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put on the powders a piece of plaster of gum or other plaster holding strongly, and let it be until it adheres by itself, then cure with oil until it is healed;
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of the suture is that you assemble the wound:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have made you know.
des apostemes des levres	of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	In some men there are dense hard abscesses on the lips resembling seeds of vines, and smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then it is necessary that you pierce the lips, and make an incision on each knot, and take them with forceps and cut in each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply to the wound after the incision a broth of vitriol, until the blood is stanched;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then anoint with oil of iris, and treat the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times there is born on the gums a fleshy growth, which the old call "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	if it is necessary that you remove it with pincers, and cut at its root, and let the gum or the blood flow;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	Then put on the limb a broth made with vitriol, or other powders which are astringent and drying.
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if the wound reopens after the incision, and often happens, if the opening is a second time, and it must be cauterized:
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not reopen after the cauterization;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of ulcers for a wound to close.
des sordens	of abscesses
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they gather at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, and are rough and bitter wounds;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes the tooth is black and yellow and worm-eaten, until the corruption reaches the gum, and the tooth is stinking;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	if it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his head be in your lap, and take the teeth or the ulcers firmly, until nothing remains;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus make from the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowness and the other stains, as long as they are moist;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes that which is in the first layer, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then proceed with the second layer and the third, until you have resolved everything;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the tooth has a need for various forms of instruments to scrape, according to what the work requires, because the roots that one scrapes from the teeth have other forms than those that one scrapes between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and let these forms and others be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay as long as you can, for one should not do it hastily;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a very high substance, so thus one has no excuse for hurrying.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained by the pain of the trait, it is necessary that you are certain of the tooth that is aching.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in the healthy tooth, and makes the bad tooth ache;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and yet the pain does not depart from that, as long as the bad tooth is extracted, for we have already seen it happen to these teeth;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are well certain of the tooth that is aching, it is necessary that you scrub around the tooth on all sides with strong spatula to guard the gum on all parts;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then rub your fingers or the subtle instruments at the first spot and spot, until it is well cleaned, then I fix the instruments well;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the head of the patient be in your teeth between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth properly without breaking it, and if it does not come out by itself, then take one of these instruments and insert it gently into each part, and move it as you have done previously.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is pierced and fragile, then it is necessary that you fill it with cloths, or where the perforations are.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you extract it subtly with pincers, so that it does not break while extracting;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to be very careful in working around the gum to avoid dislodging the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And it is good to warn that you do not break it, and leave a part behind, and cause the patient greater pain from the root's wickedness than from the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not act like the foolish barber, who through their haste and hardness sometimes break the instrument, and do not heed what we have told.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	But sometimes they come from the effect of that great disease through the roots that remain, or from the cartilage that it breaks, as we have often seen;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is pulled, then wash the place with wine or vinegar and soap;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if a flow of blood comes from it, which often happens, then fill the place with burnt vitriol;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that is not sufficient, then cauterize it;
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the instruments, which first stop the tooth, should be long and pointed and thick handles, so they do not bend when you pull the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should be of thick metal so that they do not bend when pulling, and should be made of good iron, and should have teeth to hold firmly;
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in the gum, it is necessary that you put on the spot a moist cotton in butter for one or two hours, until the gums are softened, then remove the tooth-aches which are called "algefri", from which the head seems to be ill;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and let them be made dense like a file and this is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tooth-aches, it is necessary that you discover the flesh totally around the root, and put the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a pelican, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be strong and large so that it does not break anything, and if the root jumps by itself, it is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if it does not, then you will aid yourself with all the instruments, of which the shapes come here after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one aids oneself with this instrument which has two handles, because of its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front in the root of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pincers, because of its shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let these instruments be strong so that they cannot break, and know that many tooth-instruments are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not mentioned;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise masters find by themselves their instrument, according to what their work and the disease shows them, for there are some diseases where the ancient teachers did not teach the use of an instrument because of the diversity of ills and it breaks a part of the body or the other bones, or it corrupts, if they seek the instruments that they need, which I have told you, and aid with gestures, because of its shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let it be thick and well-held to hold the bone, so it does not break, but can hold it and remove.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the limb with suitable medicines for that, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, then take all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the appearing tooth does not correspond to the natural body, and its shape is ugly, and likewise in women with shriveled breasts, then you must know if the teeth are born after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and one cannot soothe or file it:
adonques lou raie;	then remove the bone
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is stuck with the tooth, take this instrument which has this shape, and resembles a small beak, and let it be of sharp iron pointed at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut a little and a little with the forceps for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then take the file of a certain file as is its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is as if the thread of the joint makes the needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and in the joint of the tooth, little by little, it comes back lightly, so that it does not move until it heals;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the smoothness at the end of any roughness, and if the teeth are too sharp and they bite the tongue, it is necessary to file the roughness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front tooth aches, either from percussion or from cold, and the patient cannot press on it because it hurts, and you apply curative medicines to constrict, and that is of no value;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if it is necessary to constrain with a thread of gold, because the silver threads turn green and rot, but the gold does not move;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you want to thread the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the thread between the rotten teeth, if there is one or several, until you come cleverly just to the other side of the healthy tooth;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then reapply the covering just to the part where you started, and withdraw your hand subtly and cleverly, so that it does not move at all;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the ends of the thread to one width, and assemble them, and push them between the healthy tooth, and put it in so that it does not bite the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	And then let it be constricted as much as it can remain, and if it comes undone, or the threads are broken, then constrain it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if it remains and serves in this way all its tension, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the arrangement of the upper teeth and lower teeth, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when a tooth falls out, then reset it in its place, immediately, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and do not interfere with it, for it is not wise and painful, and sometimes one makes the shape of a tooth from cow bone, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and constrains it as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper, the ligature of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes there are ligatures that come from under the tongue or palate, which one is born with;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	from an accidental deep wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold their head in your hand, and lift their tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the nerves of the tongue, as long as it is dislocated from its support, and if there is hardness or swelling, and it is due to a sudden wound, then cut the ligament and cut from the length that which binds;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and beware that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery that is beneath;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done this, raise the limb of a warm and dry cloth, or a cold one, then put under the tongue a piece of linen;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and tie the patient's every night, so that their limbs cannot move.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if a flow of blood comes, then put on the limb a bandage of vitriol;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if it is not seen, then apply the cautery to the cautery of Lentigo, which is good for that.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat with another treatment until he is healthy,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see the flesh of a bad color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is cancer;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it declines to a flux, and there is moisture, then he will vomit the phlegm, and make a subtle spatula, and deliver it from one side and the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if it is not seen in your work, then put on a warm broth of vitriol as long as it is constricted, then return to your work as long as you treat everything thoroughly;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then raise the limb from clay and from stool, and treat with other treatments until he is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Certain times there come within the throat mouthfuls which are called "godath", and we properly call them the II manders, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healthy, take heed:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if it is a hard abscess of small size and of dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and its root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also because of the discharge of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it be until it becomes ripe, and then you will cut it, where it would break apart by itself;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of white color and rounded, and its root is subtle, then prepare the instrument for cutting, but first check if the abscess is warm and is at rest.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his hands in your hand, and open his mouth and press the tongue down with all the instrument, so that this is its form;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and let it be of silver or subtle brass as with surgical knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	When you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, if you take the onion and the fig in the hand, and pull it far up more than you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and pull anything from the tonsils with it, then cut it with the instrument, so that this is its form, which seems like a strong force;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and all the way the head is curved, and one part to another, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or of steel;
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then cut the tonsils with scissors, so that this is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And let it be cut from one side, and named from the other.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have cut one of the mandibles, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and water and sitz bath, and if there is discharge of blood, gargle the patient, or decoctions of cooked pomgranates, or fumigations of myrrh, and similar things, until the wound is stanched;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then anoint the cure as long as it is healthy;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and sometimes there grow in the throat other abscesses besides the two mandibles, then cut them thus as the two mandibles equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had grown inside her throat, to be sure the abscess of small size;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and it had completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and she could not eat or drink, and would have been dead if she had stayed like that for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses were so high that they had put out two wounds through the two openings of the nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I delayed then so long, and fixed in one of the shoulders, then pulled out the arrow, and with it a large portion of bone;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I reset the other part through the other opening of the nose, and I opened her mouth and I pressed on her tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	after I fixed the shoulder in these abscesses, and I cut away a part of it, and from it came out only a little blood;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the passage of the throat was unclogged for the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease to cut away at that abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscesses reopen often, and fill the place that I had emptied, as long as it swells very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I strangled it and cauterized it within the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	unless it stays without growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and may I be separated from these parts, and may I not be but what God made after me.
de l’uve	of the egg
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When humor descends to the egg, and it is inflamed and it is long, then it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is irregularly thick and round, then it is called "egg".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is purified as we have said in the division, and the purification does not profit me, and you see that the painful abscesses are alleviated, and it is subtle, then it is necessary that you cut it;
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is rounded and assembled is not too long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or of a dark reddish color or black, then you should avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we made mention of previously;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the needle into the hole, and draw it back, and cut with one of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cut except for the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cut too much, you will harm the voice and the speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, make use of what we have said about the treatment of the two arms, and treat it until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has pain in the navel, then you must use a needle for the cauterization of the painful area.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is a sharp point.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient puts his head in your lap, and then you press the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and constrict it with a living needle, so that it is not too thick nor too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and fill the cavity of this instrument, according to its shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And have near the head a cloth where medicine is put, like the contents of a spoon, and put the instrument with all the medicine on the wound;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should sit on their side, so that the saliva and the mucus running from their mouth of the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the abscess;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the abscess, for a quarter of an hour, until you see it become numb and the irritations of the medicine are alleviated;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton on the skin above, until the cotton adheres to the abscess;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry, and apply a plaster afterwards for 3 or 5 days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you have need to repeat the cauterization of the medicine, then repeat it, and after the cauterization spread cotton around the abscess, in butter, and cleanse that which is around the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be treated with cold water, and let it be cured of gargling as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than the incision, nor is it like the cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calament and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and arvnne and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in a pot, and put it to boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well plugged with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot there should be an instrument made in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And let it be of silver or of copper, and let one of the ends be placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapors rise to the eye through the reed, until the eye is numbed;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	After the recovery often happens, as long as the abscess is dry, and beware that you do not cause this at the beginning of the treatment of the hot abscess, for many things happen;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not apply heat except at the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if a suitable instrument is not available, then take a cane and put inside the top a tuft of wool, so that the mouth of the patient does not have too much heat;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the tuft of wool does not let the hot vapors harm the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with salt.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times it happens at the throat or spine or fishbone, or some other thing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so it is necessary that you pull out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and that which does not appear and is thrown back into the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the food is cut in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	by chance if the thing passes through the vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of navy, or a root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie to the sponge a thread, and then swallow it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the level of the liver, if it sticks, and then pull it out with force;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out from what we have said, take the instrument of a plum in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised high;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and beware that you do not touch the diaphragm, lest all of it comes, nor do you perforate the inside of the bone;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is good that the patient should expel the mucus, because it will be better for them or the thing will be easier;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if it falls downward, or it pulls equally throughout the entire instrument, as long as it is outside;
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Each time the blood is treated with medicine, as I have said in the section, by the treatment of remedies;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when this does not profit at all, then look in the throat of the patient to the sun, then press the tongue with the instrument that I have told you;
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, if it pulls to the smallest finger, or to the subtle tendons that are worth this;
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that is not effective, take a heated iron, and insert it into the patient's throat, then apply the iron to the tonsils, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a high fever every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full draught of cold water, and open the mouth, and let it run down the throat, and move it with the hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if the blood vessels feel the cold, then spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not spit as we have said, then fumigate the patient with assafoetida, through the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the urine;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, for it will discharge without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of the fumigation is that you take a pot where there are hot coals, and it be covered with a perforated cloth in the middle, and through this hole be the head of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then give fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not go out, but comes just to the wound;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the wound will heal now, and if it does not heal, then resume the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and let the patient fast, and abstain from salty and foul things, and not drink any water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it will be useful for the fever to be expelled through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the wound, is, when one can see it, similar to curved tongs by means of which one enters into the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and has resemblance to a hawk's beak, and has roughness of a file, so that what it takes, it cannot release;
et vez ci la forme:	and see to the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what memory recalls hereafter in this book, and they differ in perforation and in cutting;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two ways of which one is in its own likeness, and that which it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the limbs where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the flesh are different from those that come in the joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if an abscess one should not pierce, as long as the bone is measured according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are swollen, and do not measure according to their completion, like abscesses which are near the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from the joints, and one lets them be for as long as they are enclosed within, by chance if the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Or when the abscess is within the main limb, and you delay the perforation until it becomes ripe, then it will harm the main limb;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or if it is in the foundation, one should pierce it as soon as it is ripe;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is necessary that you pierce the abscess after complete digestion, unless it is the one that is in the foundation, so that it does not become putrid deep within, and be enlarged inside, and a fistula develops;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the time for perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to completion, and this is when the pain is eased, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and of the redness, and the decrease of the swelling and of the anguish of the head of the abscess, and other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you make a seat for the perforation or more dependent on the abscess, and where it opens wounds;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and let the perforation be of the length of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and veins and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no point of plethora.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that are full, according to whichever member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in the carnal part, it is of use to let the perforation as long as it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you make a hole before that, the body will be fed by its own venom, and it will be full of much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and they ulcerate the lips and the depths of it internally.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if on any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limbs need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you put small plasters on small abscesses, small perforations;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and on large abscesses, large perforations, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if in such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the head, and cauterize;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become jaundiced like the liver, and is numb, then it is necessary to do as one does for buboes:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if of such ones that are cut into three angles, and if of such ones where one cauterizes like the spleen, as abscesses of the entrails;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if of such ones where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cauterizations.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head to the abscess, like a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce the skin plainly;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscesses are large, and they collect much pus, and you will pierce, but do not drain the entire pus at once, rather drain a part of it;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop up the abscess with a poultice until the next day, then drain some other thing of its own kind;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times, a little at a time, until all the pus has come out;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	especially if the patient is of weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old and decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the blood vessels are sometimes torn with the issue of the pus, so that by accident the patient dies, and you do not perceive it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Finish this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound is small, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it's a flat incision, then apply bandages of linen or cotton threads;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it's a large abscess, and there are many openings, then it is necessary that you put a bandage on each one so that they touch one against the other;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have shaved around it, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or with linen wrappings without moisture, and bind it tightly for three days;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then anoint it, and treat it with oil until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there are evacuations of blood in your work, then apply cold and watery water, and wet the cloth, and put it on the affected area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the hemorrhage of blood persists, then apply governance and treatment, and the powders that I mentioned in this book, and if it is in the time of winter, and the limbs or abscesses are very nervous, then it is suitable to put on tents and moist dressings with wine and hot oil;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in summer, and the limbs are fleshy, then it is suitable to put on moist dressings with water and oil, or wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then unwrap the abscess and the dressing and the treatment, as it is suitable, until it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this is suitable to know universally in treatments of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	that I have said how one should proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and see it in this chapter.
des soros	Of the sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or there are small abscesses coming from the head, and they are manners of us that are in tiles, just like the joker of a dice, and many have similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There is some fat and such things where there is moisture, just like in poules;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if there are such things that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no point of doubt that the artery is not made contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the cut is that you will test all the instrument which is called "incising", from which the shape comes after, whatever thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then it will be done by those from the length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is evacuated, then one scrapes without leaving anything the skin which contains that moisture, for it returns immediately when one leaves nothing;
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then plunge cotton into Egyptian ointment, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, in the vein and in the wax, and apply to the wound, and leave until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and cauterize those who have remained with nightly discharge.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then replace the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that no discharge remains;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound with ointment suitable for it, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if there are abscesses that hold in fat, then cut around it in this manner, from the length;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and cut your lancets, and scrape all around, and put all your treatment to draw out the pus where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery has made a constriction, then do what I have told you after;
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for the abscess if it is stone-like, and to cut and to cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut into the stone-like abscess and the moist one, if it is lighter, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if in some of these abscesses or head where there is no moisture, and of these abscesses that I treated on the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the abscess as hard as a rough, harsh and white stone, and could not break it;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had struck it with iron, one would have made a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming on the head, that is those which come on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should be so always dependent on the bowel, because of the proximity to issue the mouth;
et les cure si com il covient.	and the treatment if as it suits.
des scrophules	of the scrofula.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times there are abscesses on the neck, and below the shoulders, and in the corners, and sometimes they come to other parts of the body, and are many, and are stuck together one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly within its own area, as the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and there are many similarities among these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and some which are malignant that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one then you see of good disposition in the body, and is similar to the color of the body, and moves from each part and does not numb the shoulders nor the arm nor the artery nor the vein, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	If it happens that you cut through the skin, and strip away each part, and the two lips of the wound are like a razor's edge, you are in this profession, as we have said concerning abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and you touch a little and a little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and it is not suitable for the spatula to be cutting, lest the hands tremble, and do not go too far, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and that does not stop the bleeding, then put on the wound vitriol ointment, or some powders that staunch blood, and bind the wound;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and let it be until the abscesses are relieved, and the wound is softened, and begins to decay.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stanched, it returns to your work, until you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then look at your hand to see if there remain small scrophulas, and cut and mend them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrophula, it is not advisable that you cut that scrophula at its root, but rather tie it with a strong double thread, and let it drop by itself, without harm;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then the cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire scrophula, it is advisable that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, so that there is no remaining excess because of the size of the scrophula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is advisable that you understand to cut at the root of it, and pull out strongly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrophules that hold a suppurating flux, pierce it where it appears most open;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce it as was said beforehand, in dependency, then I will apply tents with ligatures and similar things, so that it corrupts that which remains of the corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, then apply the treatment of ligature greasing with charcoal, until it becomes healthy.
de squinance	of the ankle
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The old ones spoke and talked about the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw in our land anyone who did it, and it is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have a fracture of the ankle, it is necessary that the fissure of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be examined;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and one should not make aid by that, because all the veins and the tumor of the disease are in those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in both arms.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the throat, it is necessary to operate on the epiglottis to prevent the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary, then, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we make a small incision of three or four circles, or through the quantity of the incision of the surface, between the two circles, or by the quantity of the incision of the membrane, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those places are suitable for the section of the epiglottis where there is no point of cartilage, and the vessels are long with it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to its full length, then cuts the tissue as far as it comes to the gullet.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and guard against the blood vessels, if you see any thing, and then cut the surface, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the cut of the vein of the kidney that the blood jumps through the limb which is broken, and by the deficiency of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and let the wound be covered with a dressing.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed for which one doubts the strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew them entirely without touching the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Do not give this treatment as long as the throat is completely obstructed, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the defect is in the spleen.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut through the epiglottis for that which the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and therefore the old ones command to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or in four, and then they command to cauterize the wound and treat it, until it is cured;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took the knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the tendons from the forearm;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called by the healer, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had flowed from it, and saw that she had not cut a vein or a pipe except for the throat, and the veins had burst outside through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed the wound, and treated her until she was healthy;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it happens at the lady's fury that she was hoarse of voice, and returned afterwards to her condition;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for two days that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no pain.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "throat hernia", and it is a big abscess in the color of a jaundice, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it occurs in two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or natural does not have a clear origin.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is in two manners, one of which is similar to fatty tumors, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from a vein artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and it does not cause pain, and it is not necessary to make fire cauters except in that which is small, and prove and examine the entire intestine:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you treat it thus with a greased cloth, and do not apply to any vein, if you cauterize, as one cauterizes the nails, and touch everything with its wrapping, if there is not a point in it;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and press well everywhere, and treat it as it requires, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	of the nails
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many kinds of nails are, about which I will speak all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and therefore it is necessary that I say the entire difference that exists between a nut and an abscess.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that an abscess is heat and fever holding, as long as the ebullitions have not passed, and are accompanied by decay;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then the fever and the heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With a nut there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains ichor, which is its own special humor, and is according to the color of the body, and grows like a cyst, and becomes large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to II similarities, or hot, or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the wound, that you examine and inquire first about all the instrument which is called "entromissoire", according to what its form will be or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring about the abscesses of the wounds is that you take the most moist part that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, as long as you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then it is according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the entromissoire, and take heed in that which the blood escapes.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs short, which color it has, thus do as I have said regarding other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and after the intermuscular area comes moisture, be aware that it is fatty, then make an incision in the form of a cross, and take the pincers, and lightly scrape each part and observe the skin where you think you should draw it with the needle;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it with a thread, then draw it by pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, it comes back to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a little remains, and the blood does not stop, then fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, and hold the wound, and apply hot apostumes to calm it, and treat it with other treatments until it is healthy;
