et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, then sew the two lips of the wound, and treat it with those things that promote scarring.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the veins are beating in a contrary or other manner hasten and apply the vitriol ointment to the limb, and let it stay two or three days, until the wound suppurates, and the evacuation of blood occurs;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to the copper vessel that which has been left from the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of the entromisaire instruments, and they are of three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	large and medium and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three kinds which are called "albarets", and one which is called "breb", and they are of three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, for investigating the abscesses of fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one cuts the splinters, and they are of citrin or iron, or silver, and those that are tawny are worth more, and are more tested for probing the cavities of fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three manners:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The forms of the ulcers are of many similarities, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if there are ulcers that have two concavities of three kinds also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if there are ulcers that have three concavities, and they are also of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if there are ulcers that have two concavities, and ulcers with only one concavity, and they are of three kinds;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all this is necessary in their body.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these, which one makes, are cutting, and of such that do not cut more than from one side, from which one scrapes the knots, because one does not touch the vein nor the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these internal abscesses are the ulcers responding to treatment, so that the patient does not perceive the opening of the abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not make use of more force than in the flesh of a nut, such as thighs, and arms, and shoulders, and limbs, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling the scraper of a fistula, according to this form, with which one scrapes blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes at the place that bleeds from cutting of veins, and arteries, and sometimes they break according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the shoulders of some men become inflated when they begin to be corrupt, so that they seem like a woman's shoulders;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and let them rest and become inflamed, and whoever wants to cure them, if it is necessary to follow this form of the following line, up to the end.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicinal gum arabic, then bring together the two lips of the wound to suture, and the treatment until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast hangs low, and is swollen due to its size like it happens in women, if there are two costal prominences above, through two similar fissures;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	because one holds the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. to the line .g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about suturing and powders, and what is necessary for the treatment, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the decrement of blood, then you must fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And let it be until it reaches the mucus and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that occur under the armpits are kinds of hard tumors or knots, and in which there is contained moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those therefore that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line B to line G:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the whole boil that is in the abscess is emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton, and let it be until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with pleasant ointment as much as is needed until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrophula, they make them as we have said in cases of scrophula, and if the wound is deep, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin that is above it becomes swollen, then often come abscesses, and similarly it happens to the swollen vein and abscess;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows that it is because of the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your fingers, feel for the strangeness;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is because of the vein, then the remedy appears clearly;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cut this abscess, and likewise when it is beneath the shoulder and arm and near the neck and in many other places, and it is very serious.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is necessary then to avoid the treatment of iron, and he who is in charge must avoid it also, and in the one who has an arterial hemorrhage caused by a blow from above the skin for a long time;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then make an incision at the groin of the wounded, and carefully separate the artery from the tendons, until it is exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then push a needle through the wound, and have it pierced to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then touch the limb that is between the two threads of an intermediary, as long as the blood flows from it, and let the abscess be opened;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then bring together the edges of the wound that gape, until the thread holds;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the joints having reached this point, as long as it is healthy;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is the size of a vein, then you must hold in your hand what you can from the abscess to all the skin, then push the needle under the skin that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and have a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then sew up the abscess, as I have told you, or tie one of the two parts with two threads around the head of the thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will not come loose, then rethread another needle with all the thread under all the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and pull the threads in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess as long as the superfluity goes out, then cut the superfluous part of the skin and leave what is tied;
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on a dressing of warm wine and oil, then apply treatments of bandages and bindings until it is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of the abscesses of the kidneys
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come into the artery and in the vein, abscesses come to the kidneys when they are injured, or from too great exertion, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this often happens in the joints and in the fingers and in all the limbs where there are joints, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color seems like the color of the body, and is in many cases without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one extracts it forcibly, the patient feels pain, and it is not in the depth of the body, but rather near the heart;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and it moves well in all directions, and does not go either forward or backward, nor up nor down, and that which is in the joints does not need to be cut with iron:
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	By chance it comes to contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and those who are at the head or at the forehead, make the skin spatulate.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscesses are small, if you hold them with tweezers, and cut at their root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, if you hold it with forceps, and scrub it, then you wash and bind the wound to the suture, and cure it until it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	thick hanging cheeks
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Sometimes it happens in the belly and not in any other part of the body, and it is an illness which is called "fungus" due to its resemblance to mushrooms, and its root is subtle, and its head is thick;
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and it has small and very large ones;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw a man who had two in his belly which looked more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were slightly split, and they corrupted continually with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cleaned and found in one eighteen ounces in weight, and in the other six ounces, and the work of cutting if it is that you examine the patient's moisture, and the color of the joint is white and moist and of subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if he applies the spatula to the large wound, and in his presence is the cauterization by fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For in the cutting comes often too much flowing of blood, and if it does not stop itself, then you should hurry to cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient is faint and fearful of the incision with iron, take a well-made thread, and tie the joint as we have said, and let it be for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then restrain it, and do not cease to tighten the thread of the splint as long as it covers the joint, and holds it without effort;
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are thick, then fear not to cut through the middle for the belly, but you can well cauterize half of it, then the cautery so that it does not grow back;
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cure the wound, and beware that you do not cut the tendon which is of fixed color and of little sensation and of slow regeneration.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an enlarged abscess, and I will come to the treatment of cancer later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the navel is ruptured
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the navel comes from a cauterized wound or a crack in the skin, and it is on the belly and in some of the navels, as it happens in other ruptures, or of blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is through the rupture of the skin and the exit of the navel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and is a light thing without pain, and open to various discharge.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestine, then it is even more serious, and when one presses on his sides if they bulge, and then return, and by chance if it closes, and greatly increases the pain of the bath and through strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it's a light matter, and it opens well when you press on it with your hand, not constraining anything;
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it is due to blood, then it opens through these signs of a large and hard abscess, and is fixed according to a quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to flatulence, then it is enough to touch, and the work is such that you consider its appearance by the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have said to you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is in the intestine or the navel, then it is necessary that you instruct the patient to stretch his belt, and be entirely straight, then sign from the bottom all around the navel;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then instruct him to sit comfortably between your hands, then go around the place that you have signed with all the spatula, then stretch half of the abscess upwards with all the large uncle;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then bind him around with a strong thread, or with a cord of strong chain firmly, and be the one who holds the bound limb;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open half of the abscess stretched on the limb, and thrust your right index finger, and touch the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it taken by the limb, then untie it, and thrust the intestine to the bottom of the belly;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bowel, take it to the ankle, and cut away the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein makes a counterincision, then go gently within, next return to your work and take two needles, and push two threads, and put the two needles within what you have made in the shape that you make perforate;
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then strain the abscess in four places under the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and let the limb alone until it forms a scab, and separate the dead flesh by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or cut it when it has become thin and formed a scab, then treat what needs treatment, and drain the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and strain the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the limb for what it needs, and bind the limb.
dou chancre	Two sores
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have spoken in the division of the similarities of sores, and how one should operate with medicines, and how one should choose the treatment with iron;
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and let us say that the sore is born in the marrow, and there is great caution in the treatment, and the ancients said that when a sore is in the blood or where one can raise it like a sore which is in the limbs, and in the thigh, and in similar places, and it must be completely removed when it is at the beginning;
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, it is not necessary that you approach it, for I have never known any healthy outcome;
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	nor did any of them heal in my presence.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the treatments, when it is in the blood or where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you should purge the patient of black bile;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	Then make him sweat if he has shown retention, then prepare the patient's body for the operation;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then cut his tumors or cancer, and shave him completely, and strip the bone of everything on all sides leaving nothing behind;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and squeeze the body well with your hand or with something, and if the flow of blood is against the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it as long as the blood is stagnant;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal him with another healing until he is healthy.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have already said in the division the symptoms of dropsy, and in what manner the gathering of the fluid is made, and the signs of each symptom, and the treatment that is done with medications, and that which is treated with iron:
si est eclites soulement;	It is broken only by the ankle;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one must not touch iron to these two similarities:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	it is to know, tympanites and yposarche, for it is mortal things;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	then when you apply medicine to this similarity of dropsy which is called "broken" of medicines, and the cure does not benefit, if consider that the patient is weak, or if they have another disease besides dropsy, such as a tumor and a solution of stomach and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	if one does not touch it with iron, for it gives doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient with strong virtue, and they have no other disease except dropsy alone, and they are neither too young nor too old, then you should thus proceed:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	raise the patient upright on your hands, and let the attendants press the stomach inwards curving the needle to the lowest part of the chest, then take the spinal instrument spiny according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be a cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	to the point, and the intestine should not be so entered that it can come just to the intestines when one puts in the needle, and it cannot be stopped;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then look if the dropsy is turned towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if it is necessary that you split into the belly three fingers deep just above the navel;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the dropsy is from the illness of the liver, let the incision be on the left side of the belly three fingers;
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is from the spleen, let it be on the right, and it is not necessary that the patient put on the incision that the superfluities do not run to that weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and the belly, and raise your hand to all the spatula between the skin and the inner layer as in scraping according to the quantity of a nail or an inch;
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Then pierce the skin as far as the spatula will reach to the empty space, and it is the place of the needle, then pull the thread, and I throw this instrument from which this form is made:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it resembles a thin chain of silver, and is made from fine iron or brass, and has on the lower part two small perforations;
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on one side, three perforations;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on another side, and one on another;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the head is cut like a quill, and it is the shape of the incision that the scribes sharpen the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at its tip is the needle, so when the thread comes to the needle, it descends now onto the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	guide it then to the middle or the third part, for if you guide more than is necessary at that time, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his arm's spirit, or he becomes pale, or he approaches death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but in emptying according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to that which the dispositions of the virtue of the disease signify, and its pulses;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then draw the instrument and hold the needle, and it is held now by the cord that stops up the perforation which is on the surface, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then introduce the instrument on the other side, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw from the needle a small quantity;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	make it on either side, and guard yourself from touching as long as there remains only a little of the needle.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt regarding the patient, and you leave much of the needle, if the treatment of the tomb or abscess is hot, and by very sweating or bath and in the sun, and if it tinges with a black color;
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the treatment of drier medicines as long as it is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the needle, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the flow
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who do not have an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it happens that he has to pierce through the entire diaphragm with a very subtle instrument according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then put in the hole a fine tube of lead, and tie it with thread, for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, let the hole be opened, and let him urinate, and then put it back;
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and by accident it happens that there is no stop, because the urine that comes out does not allow it to be closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those with small wounds, it is a medicine of pennyroyal clay, as we have said, which will widen them.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the wound in their body are crippled, because none can urinate who have the wound at the head of the penis, for they cannot urinate before they lift their penis up high;
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot have an erection because the material cannot come to the marrow, and it is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the work is that the patients sit on their back, put their hands under the head of the penis and the thighs like the width of a penny, so that the wound gapes in the middle, as it ought to be;
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and beware of the effusion of blood that comes many times, and if it happens, stop the flow of what flows blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	The blisters of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times a cyst appears on the penis, and it is an appearance of painful flesh;
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and it has both malignant and non-malignant types;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	if necessary, you should take them with a subtle onion, and cut and cleanse all of them, then apply cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment;
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with ointment of diafoin until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the cyst on the penis is malignant, of foul color and putrid, then you should apply a cauterizing agent.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have cut it, and the cyst is on the penis, and has one part inside the skin and one part outside, then you should remove the cyst that is inside first;
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when it is removed, then treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you treat them together, if the head of the rod is not secured so it is not perceived, and blackness and corruption come in the rod and in the body.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply on the plaster made of honey and flour which is made from the crust of green raisins and figs, then treat with other treatments until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a flow of blood comes from the ulcer, then apply the lunar cauterization according to this method:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cauterizations help in two conditions together:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	that is to say, for the flow of blood, and for the corruption;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the rod is corrupted and withdrawn, then it is necessary that you put or conduct on the rod a chain of lead, and urinate the patient amidst;
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the skin is pulled up to the head of the penis in those who have not been circumcised, or it has been due to a wound or an abscess, then you must scrape it with a sharp instrument, until the veins are loosened and the head of the penis is freed from all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if it is a grievous thing to divide this, then you must scrape it with the spatula of some iron at the head of the penis and of the skin;
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then separate them gently between the two, and put a subtle cloth of linen moistened with cold water, so that it does not adhere to the flesh.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a separation of continuity like other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	in every way when we do this work of our will, and especially with children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention the circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have no more than what we have acquired through experimentation.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen the greatest part of the masters and surgeons who performed circumcision near my home, with force, and to everyone it was a novelty;
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	If the heart was affected because it has two titles, and by chance if one takes from above and remains below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	When copper is recovered, and the pain is double, and in the purification that is given from there it is not assured the point of the member;
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and in the purification of the nail by chance the iron is sharpened, and the work is run, and many times it happens that they have no need for purification and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the purification that is done with force to everyone, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well from above as from below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if you cut it evenly throughout all the tissue;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the thread should be well pulled inside the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and let the method of the first work be that you make the child think, if it understands, that you do not make it think to tie the thread inside the stick so tightly, and then you make it come out in all the ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then you make it stand straight between your hands, and you press the fractures between your hands or under your feet where the child cannot see them, nor any of the instruments;
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	then you put your hand on the stick and blow into the wound, and pull it upwards as long as the head of the stick is inside;
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	then you clean it well of the pus that has accumulated, then tie the limb securely with a double thread, then tie it under one knot to another knot;
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and pull it with the two fingers by the second finger on the thumb and the index finger, and between the two tendons, then lift the heart of the hand upwards slowly and draw the head of the rod;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow little by little, for it is the remedy;
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on it and on the powder a plaster made from a mixture of egg whites cooked tempered with water rose, jammed with rose oil good and fresh, and let it be until the next day, and treat with another treatment as long as he is unhealthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of the dressing for the wound healing is this:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two sides be even and be cutting, and the sides be as large as the same width;
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	the defect of the healing is when the heart of it falls to the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Then it is necessary that you stretch it to your finger, so that the limbs make an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, tie it with bandages, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if it lasts for three days, and the swollen area beneath the bladder is inflamed, let it be until the abscess that is to be drained is ripe, and the crust is lightly scratched;
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	if you cut it as you can move, and guard against the area of the bladder, this will not harm him much.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Heal then the wound of things that are burnt with powder, which we have said to treat with powders, and if one cuts beyond measure, and it goes to the sinews, it will not harm;
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heal then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to obstruction of the stone, or of congealed blood, or of the bowel, or of dead flesh, or similar things that we have mentioned in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine is not discharged, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is in the neck or collar of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent over on his knees;
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and his feet should be placed on a support and his belly should be stretched from the back to the upper part of the back, and the patient should restrain his arm as much as he can;
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then the neck of the bladder is constricted by the pressure of the stone from above, for which reason the urine is discharged;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer an extraction with all the instrument called "syringe", of which this is the form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and let it be of subtle refined silver, like the down of a bird;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and let the length be a palm and a half, and let it be subtle at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the method of the emission of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie at the head a small ball of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut the excess of the wool and shape it just to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and with egg white, and make the patient sit on a seat, and rub the bladder and the rod with moistened oil of olive and of rose and of sweet almond;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently put the syringe in the rod, until it comes to the root of the rod, then bend the rod upwards towards the buttocks;
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then push the syringe up to the bladder, and let the patient feel it approaching the empty space, and this is not done according to this order unless because what conducts it there goes awry;
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then insert the thread into all of the wool little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it outside, and make the urine flow;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and continue with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When crusts or blood come into the bladder, or decay is assembled, and you see distillations of sharp things and medicines, thus make all the instrument which is called "clyster", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and has three openings:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	On one side, and on the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the limbs are shaved by which the medicine is cut so that it strikes the stick well without addition, if one can then pull out the moisture, and strike when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see that your medicines are in the bladder, put the head of the cauterizer into the moisture, and pull to the pulling one that is inside;
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you pull the moisture with the cauterizer, and then strongly strike the pulling one inside;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	if the moisture enters inside, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of the subtle syringe with which one injects into the bladder:
si est ci:	it is thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is of silver or gold, and the head is higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and touches to the brain where the ligaments are;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you want to use to clean the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts forming a double thread of wool, and heat this moisture on the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then put the end of the cleanser in the rod, then stretch your hand on the bladder to extract all the moisture completely, until the patient feels that this moisture has gone into the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you don't have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make a circle with it, and pierce it all around;
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then put a strong thread through these holes, then join the circle as one joins a bowl, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it with the instrument;
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do as you have done with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already spoken in the division of the ways of stones, and extraction together with medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and have said the difference between the stone in the kidney and in the loins, and all the symptoms, and in which stone one should open with a cut;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the rod;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is formed in the bladder often occurs more frequently in children, and it's a sign that the water of the bladder escapes similarly to water in its subtlety;
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it openly hurts, and scratches the patient's rod, and it pinches many times, and then becomes numb;
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and at the bottom of these wounds the foundations
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and the healing of children is light until they are 4 years old, and it is very grievous in the elderly, and it is like the middle age, for those who are between youth and old age;
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the treatment is lighter for those who have a large stone, than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with a purgative, to expel all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes hinders one from passing the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and bend and move to the bottom, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from the high place;
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declined downwards;
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then touch the wound from the inside;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel it in the spinal column, hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not gush out on touching everywhere, anoint your right index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is an old man, or your right middle finger, if the patient is a young adult;
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and put it in its foundation, and touch the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, if it leads to the neck of the bladder;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press on with your finger, and put it in the depth where you see fit to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch out with his right hand the intestines upwards, and with his left hand hold the skin which is beneath the intestines in the area where the incision is made;
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then he wraps the spatula with a bandage, for that is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And make between what is between the intestines and the fundament, not in the middle but on the left side of the navel;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and let it be straight on the stone, and its two ends be either at the navel or fundament, and let the width of the strap be such that it is wide outside, and narrow within, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	by chance the press so that its end which is at the fundament, it goes up without effort;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there is a piece of stone where it has edges and margins:
si est griés a issir;	thus it is prepared to exit;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if the piece which is under, resembles a pebble, and is round, of which the discharge is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	In the area where there are angles and margins, make the incision larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not heal, then you must drain through the bandages which are as tight as a lime on the head, to squeeze the stone so that it does not burst;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you apply underneath the subtle curved instrument to the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot introduce it thus, then enlarge the hole a little, and if the blood does not come out, then squeeze with the glass tube;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there is more than one stone, then put the largest first in the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull downward, and the smaller ones afterward if there are several;
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then you must operate, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For these things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	Where it dies, or the urine comes repeatedly through the leg because the kidneys cannot filter;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but you exert yourself to pull, or to tear apart the tendons, until you pull it by pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, then fill the wound with incense and balm and dragon's blood, and strain it, and apply on top a moistened cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to appease the hot abscess;
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then raise the patient up onto his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, anoint the limb well with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of galbanum and ointment of basil, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if abscesses and ulcers come in the wound and corroisons of blood in the bladder, and urine is retained by this means, which is retained in such a way that without exit with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Then put your finger in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder, and rot it;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then elevate the wound from water and from pus, and help it in all the ways that you know, until it is healthy;
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is necessary that all the treatments you administer to him, you tie the two thighs together, and apply the medicines on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if his skin is small, and it is conducted by the penis, and stuck in, and the urine cannot exit;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the treatment of what I say thus, that you often cut it, is excused from cutting because of this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proved it thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take the iron instrument in this form and let it be with three angled points fixed in one piece:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take the thread and tie it around the edge of the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then push the instrument into the edge gently, until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the instrument with your hand in the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	if urine comes out, then press your hand on the part that remains of the stone which is inside the edge.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it is thus broken, and the stone comes out with the urine, and the patient is cured;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do it for any reason that prevents it, then tie the thread under the stone and the other above, then make the edge approach the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood which is in the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal them as long as they are sick.
de la piere des femmes	of the gallstones of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It rarely happens that a stone forms in women, and if it does happen, then the treatment is grievous, and is forbidden for three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that by chance the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman who is well-informed and knows how to hide her flaws, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman who is well-informed in this art of hands;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is deeper than the stone of the man, because it requires a deeper and larger incision, and there is great danger in it. And it is necessary to have a well-informed and skilled midwife, and to take the one who has a good touch, and if you do not find one, then seek out a chaste and subtle midwife;
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and it presents a woman well-versed in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and instructs her to do what you instruct regarding the treatment of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and consider very carefully if the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then you must put your finger or foundation and seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, if the stone constricts beneath her finger, and instructs her to put her finger or with the patient, and seeks and presses her left hand on the belly firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it gently from the entrance of the belly down, as far as it comes to the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then cut into the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the womb, where it is moved and appears, and feel the stone in that area;
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and does not move his finger from the stone or the anvil, and let the first toe be cut;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then put the heat in the cut, if you feel the stone with a growing wound so that the stone can be expelled, and know that there are many kinds of stones:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	it is to know, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those that have corners.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the similarities to understand the discharge.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the blood is lacking, then put on the limb a warm broth, and hold for an hour until the blood is stanched;
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the stone is expelled, and have instruments that I have told you about in the extraction of the stone suitable for you to help with your task;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if the blood is lacking, and it is from the artery that is cut, then put powder on the limb and bind with bandages and with splints, and do not recommence this, and leave the stone and do not try to pull it, lest by accident the patient might die;
puis cure la plaie.	After the wound has healed.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is relieved, and the limbs are strengthened, it returns to its work, as long as the stone is not broken.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Rumor aqueous is nothing other than an accumulation of moisture or whiteness that is outside the heart of the intestines, which contains the egg;
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the web of the egg, if one thinks that this is another egg;
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it is the skin of the intestine between the white syfac that we have spoken of;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this humor is from weakness that comes to the intestines, and spreads that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the intestines, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it is yellowish in color declining to jaundice, or it is without redness, or black, or pale watery, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this condition, for if it is white like we have said, then the abscesses are ready, not very long like the shape of an egg, and the skin does not appear, for there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the actual tissue, then the abscesses are ready with part of the egg, and therefore one thinks that it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the intestines and the white tissue, then it smells bad;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	then when you want to know the color of the moisture, examine thoroughly all the interior quarters, from which the form is thus before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the intermission, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we treat them with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his power and the replenishment of his body;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then put him on his back, on something a little high, and put many cloths under him;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side, and instruct the minister to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the navel;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the left spatula, and cut the skin of the groin in the middle of the thigh up to near the navel, and let the incision be straight, dividing the skin of the groin right up to the white skin, and scrape subtly according to his power;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	then pierce the thin skin of water at one large opening, and extract all the water, and then put your nails, and stretch the skin upwards;
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the area of the intestines, but only the surface;
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	cut all or in pieces the membrane surrounding it subtly, that if you do not cut it well wisely, the fever will return;
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the humor rises to the top of the work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the surface;
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then assemble the two lips of the intestine's membrane to a suture, then treat it as with other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the humor corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to ligate the vessels that are suspended, in fear of the effusion of blood;
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	then cut the intestine with all its suspensions, and extract the humor, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the shoulder is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two roots;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	if you cut the other part just as you did the first equally, then suck out the blood, and put on the wound a wet linen cloth with rose oil;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put on another wet linen cloth in wine and oil, and put on the two hips, and put double blankets, and tie it up with all the linen that is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two blankets, and fill them with linen pads according to this likeness and let them be assembled by sewing on the throat of the arms, and one of the hands hold it at the base up to the back, and the other at the part of the groin;
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two ends on the shoulders, and let it be all assembled the restraint in the loop of the arm;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes this medicine of cauterization is applied to the iron in the fire, and it is that you should take the subtle cauterizing tool, and cut the skin of the intestines, and be heated as we have said, so that the white crust that contains the pus is uncovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cauterizer in this form, and pierce that crust as with needles, and scratch it with this subtle hot cauterizer:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And cut in all the ways that you can, until you scrape everything;
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and beware that the fever does not touch the eye;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is more salvage;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and beware of the flowing of blood, and doctors who are ignorant of the works of surgery;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing makes you contravened, or hot abscess or flowing of blood or other thing, then cure that which makes you contravened, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful, and does not want to undergo this treatment due to its horror, then suggest a perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well assured by the signs that we have mentioned that the cure is at hand, then make the patient sit on a raised seat;
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	Then pierce the abscess in the lower part of the entire spatula, and make the perforation as long as the body allows;
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and let the wound be wide, so that all the pus can flow out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and let the remaining pus flow out, then treat it until the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white cloth does not allow the pus to exit from the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you push a probe or instrument through which one treats the pus of dropsy, whose shape is described before;
