et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge the wound a little, and know that the edge returns, and is assembled after six months or within a year, and when it is assembled as before, then the patient will recover their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the intestines
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the cutting of this branch there is fear in many ways, for which it seems to me that moving it is worth more than leaving it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and the symptoms of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say then that many abscesses come to the body, and likewise to the intestines;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to know by the overflow of bitter and sharp humor, which is spread to the intestines, or from a blow;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and does not find a point of pain, and it is a grievous abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance is an abscess that is rough and rock-like, and of a putrid color, and sometimes comes from a swelling of the artery, or from inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from a swelling of the artery, it is recognized by the feeling of a warm abscess, when you press on it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it does not matter that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	That which is made from inflammation of a vein is recognized by its appearance to the touch of the fingers, and one can well perform the cutting on this likeness, and on the other similar things;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the skin of the intestines, then the vein is on high, and the fat tissue appears white, and delivers the suspension from all parts of the vein.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the vein is already swollen with these new wounds, then it is necessary that you treat the vein, and cut it.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is near the surface, or in that which is within the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver the entire tendon, and cut it thoroughly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the wound is in the rear of the body, then it is necessary that you cut it entirely, and extract the vein, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your tasks are completed, then apply the plaster of wool and oil to the wound, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the entrails
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess enclosed in a covering resembling a tumor, with the softening of the entrails, and the patient complains grievously when he walks;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and the treatment of this disease is as well known to be fearful as it was before, and nonetheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a seat or a bed, then tie the suspender of the thighs below to your fingers, all the vessels that are near to the privy parts, and pull the master arteries, and stretch them firmly;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	then cut with the spatula knife broadly through the skin straight across the vessels, as long as they are uncovered, and then scrape each part, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then stick a needle where it has a double thread, and tie it to the first place or where the vein has come, and tie it again at the other end;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then cut the cupping glasses straight, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupted humors;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then treat the wound like the others or where a bow is inserted, so that no vessel ruptures which would nourish one of the intestines;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	For from this comes no evil, and if all the vessels come to an end, then it is necessary to drag the intestines out through all the vessels;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and wither and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the spleen
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The coming of this flux is by the section that comes from the spleen, or the extension to the belly in the part of the loins, because the intestine descends from that rupture to one of the intestines;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this curvature is of the hip, or of the extension of it, and come these two manners from many causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or from a blow, or from a jump, or from a fall, or from the lifting of heavy loads, and from similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the symptoms when it is an extension of the hip, are that they come gradually and slowly, over a long period of time, and do not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are even up to the depth, because the hip presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the symptoms are when it is a dislocation of the hip, that it causes sudden severe pain to appear, and there are various abscesses showing beneath the skin, and it is because of the issue with the intestine and the body at the joint of the hip.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines slip with the intestine, and are retained there, and cause great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments there is fear, because it makes them want to urinate.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to push the intestine back into its place within the wound, if it can be returned.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then let it be supported on his neck, between your hands, and lift the hips;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then stretch the skin upwards, and cut all the skin of the intestines along the length;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then put within the liver of the waist, twelve inches according to that which you have in your craft for opening the wound, and let it be such that the abscess can issue out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scrape the surface that is beneath the skin of the intestines, until the white surface appears uncovered on all sides;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	then put your two index fingers in that which guides the intestine, in that which is between the white surface that is beneath the skin of the navel, and between the second surface, and separate that which is behind the navel, and between the second surface;
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and then move to the right hand inside the heart of the intestines, and let the white skin be high on your left hand, and lift the use to all the skin towards the waist;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the minister that he stretch the use upwards, and untie what is tied behind the binding;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and ask your fingers if there is a point of the intestine enveloped or white skin hardened, and if you find any thing, then push it to the bottom of the belly;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take a needle where there is a thick thread made of threads, and push it into the back part of the skin, which is after the skin of the intestines;
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	after the waist, then cut the heads that appear with threads, as long as there are four threads;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the skin with a strong thread of two parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then envelop the heads of the veins, and bind them firmly in two places, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter into them, lest the abscess that is there may grow.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put the third string according to the first string long two fingers from that one, and after these two strings leave two spaces which is two fingers from the heart of the body the size of a finger;
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and after all the other according to the roundness that the swelling makes;
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then cut in the part that is near the skin of the body, as far as the blood and the bone, as we have said before;
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then put a moist bandage in oil, and apply it to the wounds, and I will apply the string that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white skin that we have mentioned is cauterized after the incision, due to fear of excessive blood flow.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this happens often, and let the urine flow as long as it can by itself;
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it delays in coming out, then apply warm aromatics, and put on what we have said, until it flows;
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then heal the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healthy.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this condition I never saw anyone who dared to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old ones said that it is made like the branch which is next to the bladder, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after the cut above the testicles lightly with a thread;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	then cut in the middle, and treat the abscess of what has burst, until the vessels heal;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	Sometimes a dislocation occurs in the joints, as we have said, and it opens the limbs;
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and does not touch the intestines at all, to the liver, and if it touches them, it's a little, and repairs all hours;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and in any case if it stays too long in this spot, the wound or catarh grows, until the intestine touches;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens due to the extension of the catarh which is in the joints, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and swollen are the limbs and opened;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	and the cure is by cauterization, as we previously said;
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	and it is that the patient puts his back between your hands, then cut the limb of the dislocated joint swollen with a large quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the abscess that is beneath the skin which becomes apparent, then take the razor and place it on the apparent abscess;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press to the depth of the belly, then cut the two apparent abscesses on the head of the razor, and cut one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the head of the razor, and do not touch any part of the abscess nor extend the use to another thing, as I have made you know in the treatment of the ulceration of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	then heal it by the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you touch the threads, if it is infected and treat the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The abscess is constricted, and has no appearance in the routing, and the cauterizations are gentle on this spot, and closer to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the intestines
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times is softened the skin of the intestines in some men, because the guts that are inside are softened, and it is bad to see;
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, to make the patient lie on his back, and to cut the skin that is softened on the natural skin;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then bring the two lips together to a seam, and if you see, first cut away the excess of the softened skin to three or four stitches firmly;
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then cut between the stitches, and cure it like the other wounds, until it be healed, and tighten the thread.
dou chastrement	of punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Punishments are forbidden in our law, and therefore it pleases me that I do not speak of them in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and there are not necessary forces except by two means:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	where one is that the physician responds in writing when asked, and writes the treatment;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often have need of the assistance of certain beasts to aid us, such as goats and rams and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say then that chastisement is made in two ways:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	either by traction, or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one that we do by traction, we make the beast sit in warm water, as long as the bowel is softened and hanging;
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then take them with your hand, until they are put back and you do not feel them anymore.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the treatment of the cut:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the intestines with your left hand, then tie it above, and cut above each hoof with a blow, when you have well scarified them;
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and let none of the thick skin and the subtle skin which is on the vessels;
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this manner of punishment is worse than that which is done by traction, because with traction there remains by chance some thing from the gut, for which the beast desires luxury;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then heal the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphrodite is a being in two manners, male and female:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one is that between the two hips open as well as the figure of the nature of a woman, where it has hair, and sometimes the urine comes out.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has on the genital area like a penis and two hips.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the treatment of the man and the woman is that you cut the joined flesh all together, and treat it as other wounds;
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	In the second manner, of men whose urine jumps through the skin of their intestines, if there is no point of cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenderness
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Tenderness is a sore adjusted on the natural part, as it is too shameful to see;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and some women have it so large as a hand, and this is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary that you take the excess of the tenderness in your hand or with shears, and cut it lightly;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not go too deep, lest an effusion of blood does not come, then one cure does not hinder another cure as long as it is healthy;
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and there is another sore that grows at the mouth of the marrow, and the filling, and by chance breaks out, and it looks like a cow's, and for this reason the old ones call it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to cut it, as we have said the tenderness, and the treatment until it is healthy.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Erratic it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the passage is small;
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and it is natural by birth, or accidental by disease that has come to her;
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or it is by charming adjusted, or of the spleen subtle or sharp, and it is made deep in the liver, or in the sides, or below, or wherever it may be;
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and prevents conception, and childbearing, and by chance causes the flow to have;
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and the knowledge of this thing is through the examination of the urine.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears to be near the thigh or in the back.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is of the spleen subtle and sharp, and it is near the liver, then hasten, and bend the knee:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	Put your two thumbs together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs;
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then press the two fingers firmly, until the subtle skin surface becomes round, and is above the swelling;
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	then take the vein, and the mole in oil, and put it on the body, and give the woman a house remedy each day, so that she cannot suffer.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the skin is hard and thick, then it is necessary to cut it with a spatula similar to a knife blade.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the swelling is of fleshy tissue, then suck on the abscess and cut it;
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and have the blood-stanching medicines, such as hematite, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with rose water;
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	then apply a bandage of wide cloth, so that the wound cannot suffer;
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and thus let it be for a long time, and put a bandage of dry flax.
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let him be cured by other treatments until he is healthy.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marrow comes a new flesh, if it covers according to this manner, then it is not an ulcerous abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the ulcerated abscess that is in the marrow, one should not touch it with iron.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are overtures of veins which without hardening habitually, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thelul;
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have already said in the division the similarities of them, and the signs, and I will say here those which receive a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thelul, when they are deep in the marrow, and do not appear to feeling, if it is not the cure by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the abscess, one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, then stop the discharge of her menses, and cut it off at its roots, then powder on medicines that restrain blood, such as birthwort and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things;
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then let her feet soak in the bath for an hour, then put her in a cold water;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if a discharge of blood comes, make her sit in a decoction of sumach and the bark of pomegranate trees and gall and similar things, and then take flour of barley, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster to put on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it dries, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If that is not so, then have cauterized the ventoses on the back and the same for the breast;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	then take the wool, and anoint it with juice of plantain or with juice of aglentier mixed with old wine, and cauterize the body.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess has burst, then treat the body with ointment as long as it is sore;
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles the rough head, if it is necessary to scrape as I have said the tumor;
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat it until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the marrow
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come in the marrow, such as cancer and cold abscess and herpes and eczemas and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is necessary then to describe in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marrow, which is not among the abscesses that fall into a mass.
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you want to know the work of iron, look at the abscess when it begins to come, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Then do not hurry to pierce, but make me wait until the pain is eased;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then make the patient sit on a seat, and let him have two small seats or where he can lean, and support himself on his back and bring his feet together as far apart from the thigh;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his thighs be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a tight band;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then suck the abscess towards the right side, and introduce the instrument through which one sucks the marrow, from which afterwards comes the pus;
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you want to administer this instrument, that you first insert the rod to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters from the instrument does not come more deeply than it should, and that it does not harm the patient;
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instruments are larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the marrow with cloths, so that the instruments do not harm them;
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary that he places the point of the instrument upwards, and that he holds the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscesses open, and one makes an incision with a soft hand, then it is necessary to cover the head with a spatula or a plaster.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the wound is empty, then it is necessary that you put in the wound moist dressings with rose oil, or with green dry oil;
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and put the tent or dressing of strong fabric at the bottom of the wound, and put over the wound and on the bandage a clean moist cloth in water or evil humors that are cooked;
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then the treatment after 2 days of application having come to that point, as long as it is healthy;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and sometimes raise the dressing and the wound with a cluster of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lily and aristolochia that are cooked;
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then return to the application.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound has grown back onto the dressing, then it is necessary that you beware of iron cauterization, but rather treat it as we have said in this section.
de l’enfantement	of swelling
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	It is suitable first to teach the midwife that she recognize the natural signs of the swelling, and the symptoms are when you see the woman press down below, and desire to smell the air:
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	then the sinews of the infant hasten to come out;
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	and then one knows that these infant movements are according to natural design, and the issue is under its head, and the second with it;
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, then you must gently press his belly, so that the intestines protrude out;
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	for when it descends upon its head, the secondine goes with it, and the mass of its superfluities is purged by good purification;
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and that which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it comes sometimes upon its feet, and comes out of the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes upon its belly, or penis, and is turned by accident over its neck, and by other bad postures;
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	so it is necessary for the healer to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the postures as one ought to help with them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the infant comes out naturally onto its head, and the woman gives birth grievously, and the strength of the womb is weak, then make her sit on a saddle, or the women hold her;
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and let its natural oil or rennet be cooked, and then put the bath between its two legs the little spatula of which this is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and cut the second skin, and cut to one nail as much as the moisture that is in the corpse fingers;
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and press the woman's belly until the infant descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to clysterize the woman with massage of rennet with oil of cypress;
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then make her press and rub with condition, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour:
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	now the infant will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if the two hands are dislocated, then you must reset them lightly, a little at a time;
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a seat, and raise her feet up high;
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then remove the seat from the ground, and hold the woman, so she does not fall during the removal;
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if the hands cannot enter, and the infant is dead, then cut the hands at the joint that is situated here before, and extract the infant, and reset in the same way.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the infant on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the infant comes onto its feet, then it is necessary to throw upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it little by little, until it is straight;
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take one of the feet and stretch it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When the skin is healthy, if it is ordered to be pressed, and it is stretched from its natural condition;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If health is lacking, God will provide.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not lacking as we have said, then turn it little by little, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lighter.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come as we have said, then take the muscle of the wing, and oil of cedar, and melted gum, and crush all in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and apply this mixture to the woman's nature inside and outside this treatment, then have her sit in hot water until the hips are sweating;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she is moistened from below, have her wear a girdle of myrrh, and put it below, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	Then make her sit on a seat, then make her stretch out and constrain her mouth and her nose, and press her belly lightly, for the infant is coming out now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the infant upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the infant comes in this manner, thus one puts the basin of its hands little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then it should be laid on its neck, and its feet hanging down, and it should be placed on the bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and one folds its hands little by little, and then presses its hands on the belly, and lifts the cushions from beneath, until it is prepared below;
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the infant does not come out, one takes its feet and moves them forcefully, then moves the belly upward, then one pushes the hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and brings the infant little by little;
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and instruct the woman to grasp herself as much as the infant comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the exit of the child who comes out with one hand while
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if you cannot bring it back, then make the woman get up and walk;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then make her sit on the bed, and separate her legs forcibly;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then anoint the muscle that I have described;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not deliver, then make her sit on a seat, and prepare to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and turn the child according to its natural position, and make her exert herself, and instruct her to grasp herself as much as the infant comes out forcefully.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on its neck, and having expanded its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is necessary that the barber holds his hand, then turns it little by little, and lifts the eye lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, put on the natural muscle of the thigh and heel, as we have said, then instruct her to move it little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, make her sit on the seat, and instruct her to take it;
et la fai esternuer.	and make her stretch.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for the second toe
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to this manner for the second toe, cut the second toe from one nail, until the mucus is emptied;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if it swells up on its face and on its neck, cut it from the swelling, so it is not retained, and move the swellings;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, as long as you have placed it as it is necessary, and instruct the woman to take it at least once:
adonques si istra legierement.	Then one must treat it lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the issue of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	It is known that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born;
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and this is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing, and do not live, with few names;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiple, and are divided by the spleen which divides them, which is tied to the navel;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come out naturally like one entire piece, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they come out with difficulty, then the treatment is as we have said, and let the subtle bath, and make all that it does gently;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do this as it is worth for health.
de plusors enfans	Of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or many up to XV, and all are perfectly formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious sage, and it is necessary that the wise woman knows all this, for by chance similar things happen;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	thus do according to what is needed.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat the woman of the dead or stillborn child, as I have said in the section, and it does not come out, and you are forced to perform a manual operation;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is necessary that the woman be leaning on her back, and her thighs be bent downwards, and her legs be lifted;
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and let the nurse place the tie of two parts, where it is tied to the bed so that it is not treated for the dislocation of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the marrow with oil made from nutmeg and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint the patient's hands with these oils and these rubbings;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then gently push into the marrow, then choose the place where it pushes the ankles that are suitable for this, and take care that the sinews are prepared so that they come down from the head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if it fixes the ankles in his eyes or in his neck or in his mouth or in his palate or under the beard or in the jaw or near the ribs, and if the dislocation is downward towards the feet, then fix or prick there and the tender ribs;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that he pulls the elbow to his right hand, and puts the curve between the two fingers of the left hand, and bends all his hand slightly, and inserts the elbow into any of these places that we have mentioned, until it comes to the empty space;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the elbow:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then insert against the other elbow, or the third in your craft, so that the extractions are equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then stretch equally by moving from one side to the other, for muscles to exit, and let the elbows be held by muscles, as this is the shape:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if one part remains, then anoint the joint with oil from his fingers, and bend it towards that part, and pull the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there remains a point, then put this elbow or higher place, and do that until all of it comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back due to constriction, then you must wrap it in a bandage, until it becomes whole;
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	then put the cup on the joint of the sole or the heel, and thus you must do on the other hand, and on the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the head of the infant is large and it is constricted in the birth, or it has the head assembled with the shoulders, then you must put the spine between your two hands, and make the head and extract the shoulder;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you round it with the instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus same make the infants with large head naturally;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then pull the bones to the tendons, and if the head is sound and it constricts with force, it should be split, until the moisture that is in the foot issues out;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot exit, then cut it by pieces at the mouth that you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is inflamed in the belly or below the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce it as long as the humors flow.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the inflammation is on his feet, then the attraction is light, and the remedies applied to the mouth of the abscess are light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is constricted in the belly or in the chest, then it is necessary that you extract it with a cloth wrapped around the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and bind the belly or the chest, as long as the humors which are there flow;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other member is swollen, and the skin remains, then put his hand in the depth of the abscess, and pull it right up to the mouth of the abscess;
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then boil one or two onions, and rub them on the area;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the abscess is constricted by hot aposteme that has come to it, then it does not need to be lanced, but instead treated with moist and greasy things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and apply plasters, and put on soft, moistening and soothing applications.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the navel is on his side, and you can make it even, then treat it with what we have said for a living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and let no hair remain, then rub it on in pieces, and leave nothing of the second layer.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, treat it with what we have said for hot abscesses that come in the flesh;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if discharge of blood comes, then apply a restrictive dressing, and treat with other cures.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had an infant that had died, then she conceived another on top of that, and the other died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there came to him an abscess in the navel, and it swelled so much that it burst open, and began to suppurate greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought for a long time, and I could not suture the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and from it came out a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, because that which has a belly has no bones in it.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I searched the wound, and extracted many bones, until the woman was in a better state;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and I watched over the woman for a long time, and she coughed up at times a little bone from her body;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have not recounted this chapter before because of that, when the masters find a strange thing, they know how to put aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the hammer back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Then comes the shape of the presser, where one puts the pounds;
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and to two turnings at the two heads of the two tendons.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	In any case, the horns should be more subtle than the restricter, and should be made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the fist should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the trees should be two, and in length a palm and a half;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two limbs there should be two adjustements of this same fist, which should be fixed on one and on the other, a half palm in length or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and this adjustment is thrust into the mouth of the hammer for opening when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, in its likeness more subtle and lighter, should be made of wood of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of the tongs.
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and it has two arms, two adjustments, as you see, one palm in length, and two fingers in width;
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you see to open the device with all the instrument, make the woman sit on the bed, the feet hanging and the legs spread, then thrust the two adjustments joined together in the device, and hold the head of the instrument between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then open your hand with all the instrument, as you have made the tongs equally, according to the quantity that you want to open the mouth of the device, until the ball makes what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	These instruments are all elevated, and are multiplied according to their similarities;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when the surgeon has them prepared, then they are more ready for the work, and higher in price to men according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you do not have prepared, for their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained in the infant, then you must instruct the patient to retain her breath, and then make her spit out the mucus, and hold her hands at the mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she coughs through that, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, then take the pot, and make a poultice or plaster, and put in it herbs that can open the mouth of the throat, such as calamen, rue, anise, chamomile, cassialigne, and centory;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	All these herbs, or some of them, are cooked or placed in water over the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then put a cane or stick through the hole of the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the mare, and pull until the vapors come out from inside the mare;
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then make it spew, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second intestine is injured.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not purified, instruct the woman to soak her left hand in oil of sesame or in mastication of althea, and then put it in the nature, and massage the intestine;
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when she has found it, if she takes it and stretches it little by little straightly, so that the intestine does not tear at the extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but first move it lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull it;
si venra et se desaerdra.	If it comes and becomes disordered.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the stomach is constricted, we have spoken of the treatment of purging, and of the fumigation of herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not any of all that which we have said, beware that you do not falsify the treatment;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is suitable that what is at the mouth of the stomach, you should apply to the hip of the woman, then anoint her with a fourfold ointment;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if the abscess bursts and breaks, and a fever comes;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but nevertheless, when it bursts if there comes bad smell to the stomach and to the head, and bothers the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	If then suitable fumigations are applied to this:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	some of the ancients have experienced fumigation of cresson and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument by which one purges the woman of the retention of the flowers and of the secundine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is to be seen similar to a chain, and put the thin head in the nature, and the large feet on the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the purging be on the coals, and the string until it is exhausted, and recommence another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, yet the upper part is stopped up with subtle sap:
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	so it is necessary to the nurse that she pierce that upper part with her finger, and not pierce the thin membrane of the spine, and guard the ligament so that she does not touch it;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on the moist wool in wine and in oil, then the treatment of anointing until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not reset, then put or thrust a cane of plaster, and leave it there for several days, and let the swelling subside before going into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And sometimes there comes sudden swellings from a wound or an abscess;
si covient coper celui soudement:	if it is necessary to treat that swelling suddenly:
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	it should be treated, as we have said regarding the plaster cast.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that come from the bottom are an affliction, and worse than those that come from the bottom of the bowel, or in the space between the two parts, either to one fistula or several;
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when that affliction is ancient, it operates, and increases moisture with white or subtle bowel discharge, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent;
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and they are known by this, that there is vomiting or flatulence when the patient makes evacuation, and by chance in jumping or sudden movement.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if there are fistulas that reach to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and they extend to the joint of the thigh, and to the top of the hip.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And then one knows if the fistula passes into the fundament, and does not pass through:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you apply your right index finger to the fundament, and insert a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has twisting, then you insert a thread of thin flax, or a horse hair, until you feel the thread or the hair at your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come through by evacuation or flatulence or by vomiting, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	Let it be that she does not perceive anything;
si te haste dou curer.	if you hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is next to the bladder or next to the passage of urine, if it hurts the urine, and cannot be soothed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced next to the joint of the thigh, then the tendon comes near the bone;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the invention of pain within, then it is that it has thus swelling, and not worth medicine nor soothing by application;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these fistulas next to, there is no cure except for work, and vanity of foolish surgeons who get involved.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In one that is not next to and is not ancient, there is hope of health through iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient puts between your hands on their back;
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and he lifts his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined towards his stomach;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then he pulls out a tenderness of the groin, or of the loin if there is a twisting, until you know where the tenderness comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it in their gut, then you should put your second finger in, and then feel that the tenderness has been penetrated;
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if it is discovered where you feel between your fingers the liver or the flesh, then know that it is perforated;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if one does not work on it, then it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One can indeed heal some people well with it, but it happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the aid that one gives, if it is the cauterization subtle according to the width of the fistula, as it was previously stated;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and thrust all hot into the fistula, as long as it comes from beneath the foundation;
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this two or three times, until you know that these fatty tissues are burned, which resemble a feather of a bird;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat with wet tents in butter, until that fatty tissue is strengthened, then treat with a greasy ointment, and cauterizing and soldering.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	This thing, nothing else can be healed;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if it has a tent between, and does not perforate just to the finger which is at the foundation, and between your finger and the tent a thick covering of flesh or of skin, and you see the fistula in this which shows the covering of the gut;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut at the beginning of the fistula, and thrust beforehand before the tent, and then cauterize afterwards, until it comes to the head of the tent;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and the tendon will be freed, and will fall;
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then I will show you those fallen and worn-out tissues that seem like a fragment of bone, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood comes to an end, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or with a medical instrument.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the fire cauterization assembles two bony things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	it is to know, the joining of these fallen tissues, and the stoppage of blood and the drying of the moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then treat the moist tendons with a poultice or in broken pieces, as long as the limbs give a sign, and force out the fallen tissues from the body;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound of the dislocated joints with a dressing of hard material, and these are the dried medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healthy and does not relapse.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes near the bottom of the foundation, and it is separated from the body, then one must apply a poultice to the bottom or foundation, and inquire about that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tension, and between two is the web or the skin or flesh, or it is ready to pierce, if there is not a way of relief and hope, by the administration of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut near the bottom, or if you can put tents and cure as before;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep in the bottom, so that you do not cut the tendons that hold the foundation, and let the evacuations proceed according to natural intention;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then cure it, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance it will be healed, or you remove that covering and cleanse it after it has been cut from the bottom, either with a tent or with another suitable instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then anoint the wounded area with the fat that is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study how to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the part against the foundation:
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And some wounds are fistulas in this manner:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is or touches the bottom beneath the skin from above, if a thread takes hold at the head in this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I push the twisted thread into II, and push the tent with all the thread into the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it passes through the margin of the bottom from within, then pull out the thread from that which has passed, so that you push your needle at the bottom;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and pull the head of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and hold one to the other, and let it go for a day or two;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it several times, until the thread cuts through the flesh that is between them, and separates them;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treat the wound until it is cleaned and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not penetrate, then make it penetrate in all the ways that you can, if the elbow is not too deeply affected.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not suitable to make an opening through the joint if it is too deep, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spinous spongy bone from which one makes the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side not, because one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	Of the morbidities
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Morbidities are of two kinds:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are within the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and sometimes with blood, and there is one or several, and they are at the bottom of the foundation and at the head of the foundation;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are on the outside have little moisture, and sometimes with a bit of yellowish citrine or a bit of blood, and they have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them within the foundation, is that you instruct the patient to squeeze himself to urinate in chambers, until the foundations issue forth, and the threads appear;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hasten, and hold it with forceps, or you hold it on your nail, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the ulcer cannot hold with its own moisture, then take it with a cloth, or a swab, or a piece of chamel cloth.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them apart with the hands, then cut them, and sprinkle above some hot powders that are suitable for cauterization;
