ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you will cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cauterization, then treat them with other treatments until they are healthy;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot be evacuated, then give the patient a harsh and bitter suppository to wash out what is in the foundation, so that it can come out openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the sickness has taken hold, and its roots are deep in the foundation, then the treatment is difficult;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you should take them with your nail or tongs, and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healthy, and fear not the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	If it happens that you must treat the burn according to this method:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take the thread and twist it, and put it on a needle, and then pass the thread through and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two parts of the thread around the needle, and let them be of equal length;
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and pull the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and withdraw the needle, and do thus for all the others, and leave one to stop the excessive flow of blood;
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the bottom a moistened cloth dipped in oil or in cerate, and apply it to the bottom, and instruct the patient that he should rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it be until it adheres, and when they will have adhered, then treat with oil and other treatments, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Dryness of the feet or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of the feet in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is not of value.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you rest at the point of a spit or on one nail the dryness above, which does not let it be moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then cure it as long as it is swollen as it is necessary;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be swollen, then begin the rubbing again stronger than before, until it bleeds much, and is dry;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it as long as it is bleeding.
dou fremit	of a tremor
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Furuncle is a small faulty appearance in the body, and goes much deep within;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it pierces the flesh, and one feels it as if dead from a tremor, and it comes into the whole body, and more to the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a vein from a wing of a goose, or a wing of a strong culture, and put that vein on the forehead, so that the circles surround the forehead entirely;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand around the vein so that you bind everything around the forehead, and put it in the background, and clear the forehead of its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make this from a vein of copper or iron in the same form, and let it be subtle beneath and drawn above;
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	Nor pierce, for it will cause pain, and cause pressure.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, then cauterize the forehead, as it is described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cluster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Sometimes they make a cluster of silver or gold, or of melted copper or wire mesh;
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and sometimes they make some of these instruments small and large, according to what they are used for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These then are used in the treatment of children and those who are weak and suffering, and are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large cluster is spread wide, where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and it has a separation where the belly is tied, as you see, and the flesh is pierced within;
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and it has on one of its sides two perforations, and on the other one;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and the belly or bag is made with medicines of a beast's bladder or of parchment, and is pierced all around with many small perforations, and has between each perforation one thread of space, then sews into these perforations a strong thread of twisted cord in X shape or twisted around, and assembles the belly like a sieve;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, then apply a bandage in front with a strong thread, then give an enema;
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and this is the shape of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or with egg yolk, or a similar thing, then insert it gently;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then press the minister's hands together, as long as it is all seen, then remove the enema, and lift the patient's legs to their chest, and if the medicine wants to come out, hold back as long as he can;
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a night through, it is even greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give an enema for a disease of bowel decay, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it until he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the morbid matter is in the foundation, or in the abscess, it should be as subtle as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle cluster where the skin is tight:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already spoken in the section on the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	now we will tell you about the treatments with hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the limbs or wounds that are affected, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are the throwing of stones, and the cutting of swords and knives, or of lances or clubs or arrows, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made according to the limbs of the body, such as a wound that strikes on the neck, or on the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it's an injury of stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely broken and the wound is large, and you suspect slightly an abscess of heat:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if the wound is so much worse from the head injury that if it comes with a little blood from the wound, and the blood is on the contrary side of the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and forbid the patient excess of wine and of coarse meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to bleed, his food should be diminished, and he should not drink wine, nor eat any meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if abscesses or ulcers come, cotton moistened in rose oil or in tightening wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by air, powder, which I will discuss a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the blood has been moved, then put on some ointments, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be assembled by themselves with tape, then assemble them by stitching, as I will describe for wounds of the belly, concerning stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is uncovered to the bone, and it is narrow, and does not hold except for a little, then cover it;
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	After the cure of the wound with medicine, and restoring the flesh on the skin, instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as toasted and roasted meat, like pork, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find decayed skin, and it does not adhere to the bone, then cut away all the decayed part, and apply force, then treat the wound.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if an artery is in the wound or vein, without cutting, and it cannot be staunched with medicine, seek out the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and it is that you put in this powder which dries just as the arsenic treats the wound.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the method of the powder is thus:
pren encens une partie;	Take a part of incense;
sanc de dragon II parties;	blood of dragon two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	living salts three parts, and powder subtly, and apply to the wound, and extract warmly, until it is well joined and united with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then bind it well, and leave it unbound, so it does not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one makes this with salts alone, when one does not have incense or blood of dragon, but that the arsenic has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the arsenic has moved the wound, mix it in this way, then do not put any of this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some digestive ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it is entirely healed;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal other healings as long as he is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a bone breaks with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pinces.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the nerves, do not attempt any other treatment, and do not apply anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	But let the medicine be soothing, as if warm water is poured into sweet oil, and mixed with rose oil, and warm water is poured also into sweet oil, and other stones of mines according to this manner, and moistenings are applied.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is hairy and full of pus, then prick or pierce lower down;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and a flow of blood comes, then dissect, and ligate, and cauterize, it is the work of;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the vein of the throat is cut, or the artery, and the conduits are blocked, through which the food goes, then sew the artery to the rope of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then hold it in place, and let it rest for some days, then treat it with bandages until it is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, thus the cartilage;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if it has broken bones, thus the fractured parts you will treat, and that which you cannot treat, leave until the wound suppurates, and is cleansed and freed of its discharge;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have spoken of.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of a lance or of a knife cut
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a blow of a lance or of a knife, and the wound is deep, then consider from the wound what symptoms the patient has:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	Know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it with the blood that remains deep, and returns to the heart, and kills the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but I put on an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you do not have ointment, put in the wound much cotton to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound three days, or four, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if there does not come a spasm, or trembling of the heart, nor strangulation of the limbs;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the bones in their proper place, know then that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal then the teeth and other healings, as long as they are sound;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if she cannot heal, and open, then know that it is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	if the treatment is as one ought.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision of a sword or a knife, and it is simple, or in the thigh or on the back, then the treatment of that which is in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, with stitching;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and in a mass of fragments, thus cauterize the wound, and apply dressings if they are disjointed;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not disjointed, then let the wound suppurate, which will alleviate the extraction;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds of other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great and soft and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the large wound often comes out the intestine, or the nerves of the intestines, due to which is the intrusion of the guts;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the stitching is more troublesome, and often worse than the small wound that of the large one, because one puts back into place the intestines with more care, lest they be put back in a state of disorder;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestine swells as soon as it feels the cold, if they are put back with more care, and for this reason the inner wound is worse, because one puts back the intestine to its place before the others;
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And it is known that the rupture of the belly is in four manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common stitches have a place in the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of the other wounds of the body and the other proper stitches are common to the other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and all of them are more prone to the injury of the belly, and I will tell and declare each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and any part of the intestine comes out, and it's a grievous thing to put back, it is done by one of the two methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is weakened by the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is chilled, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	dampen a sponge or the belly with warm water moderately, or you heat in warm water and decoction of cypress and thyme, and rub the intestine as long as the weakness is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes do these constraining wines, and it's wonderful that they relieve by disinflaming.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the intestine departing, if it is mixed with water or oil and the wounds are poorly healed, for by this the entrance is alleviated a little of the thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a little wound at the instrument from which one takes the hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is to change the cut, that we should not cut without great necessity or need;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and these are the instruments for cutting:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if it cuts within the body and does not cut outside, and see the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out, then put it back in its natural place according to its proper form, if you have the power to do so, for this is of great value.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part near the belly, then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and the chest higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts then adjust it so that the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large and minor wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	For small wounds put that which is prepared on you, then take it between your hands and apply the ointment that you have made to all the rupture with your hand, and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common manner of stitches, and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave at the head of the wound the thread of two fingers, and attach a needle where it has a strong thread;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two sides of the leather with the two sides of the suture, which is beneath the inner leather, until you make it pierce from that part, and bring together the two ends of the suture to the four ends assembled;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then strain through a double thread within the needle of two parts, then assemble the two edges of the wound together, and then let the suture tighten, and fix another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then thread the second thread as you did the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to your skill with needles, until the entire wound is restrained.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be moderate, between fine and coarse, for fine needles take all the flesh, and those that are too coarse cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for this reason it is fitting that they be moderate;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not fitting to put the needles too far from the flesh and through the skin, so they do not take and open the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then cut the heads of the needles, so they do not bother the patient while sleeping, and put tents or dressings on the heads of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this manner of treatment is more suitable for small wounds, for it only requires a needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second treatment is common, and it is that you should assemble the two parts of the skin and the two parts of the fascia together with a needle or that it has one strong middle thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced these pieces all four together, then return the needle to the part where you began, in the manner that one sews clothes;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each stitch the thickness of a little finger;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitching is suitable for a man, and I sewed a wound that a man had in his belly, which was injured by a blow, and the wound was more than a palm in width, and it gushed out intestines as much as two palms, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I retrieved the intestine after it had been outside for 23 hours, and the wound was sewn up to the 15th day, and I treated it, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I applied cotton to the wound more than twice a day, and washed it with warm water until he was healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and pass it through the part from the outside to the inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the skin from straight to straight, then leave the head of the thread at the suture or where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce another part of the flesh from inside to outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as well as the felt maker makes the felts, and that you leave once the seam of one side, and take it up from the other, until the suture is entirely completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second manner of suturing, which the Gauls call their own, is thus: as some do, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one edge of the seam to the other edge, in a similar way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Fix a needle or head of the thread to the middle of the flesh, and make it pierce that same flesh, and leave the two edges of the seam.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the upper part just to the inner skin, at the two edges of the seam;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then make it pierce one and the other from the upper part just to the inner skin, at the two edges of the thread that are on the other stitched side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and it is the worst manner of fracture and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen says that if this symptom is shown, and no other is indicated, then one should cauterize the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew together torn things;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and it is known that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, then the stitching is more grievous than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, and the artery has moved, then put back the intestine, and the gut;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then apply the powder of birthwort, and if the artery has moved, put on some ointment that is suitable, until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and pull the thread, and let the vein be sucked, and the mucus;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with the others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you have no medicine, apply on top, just as one begins to apply goose grease, cotton wool, and rub it in twice a day until it is healed;
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no need for other medicine in many treatments when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound will not become connected to the main members, then it is necessary that you soften the leg with oil of tempered warmth, or with rose oil, and apply it between the ankles, and detach from the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if there is pain or swelling in the belly, and it often happens, then they are given a cluster of black wine, and similarly if the swelling reaches the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it pierces within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jeune" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is because of the abundance of veins that are there, and the delicacy of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to the kidneys.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the suture is healthy from the wound, then it is put back together like the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and becomes turned towards black or blue, then you must take away the black part, so that the evacuation of blood does not come, for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut what is between the ligament, and put the two bones hanging from the part below the wound until the end to alleviate the extraction when the suture is made, and the wound is closed.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the treatment of the swelling
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is wounded, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, because I have seen that a man was wounded or pierced in the belly with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right of the stomach, and it became inflamed and developed into a fistula, and thus stopped the digestion and the flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied a remedy according to what I could, and did not cease to treat subtly until he was healthy, and his limbs were sound.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him sound, I doubted that the sickness was not bad in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no pain, but remained in better disposition, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in a certain manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	Take the frenum with large teeth, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the frenum has covered the mouth, put it between the two lips, so that it constricts its mouth upon;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cut the head, and this holds so that it cannot come undone, then put another frenum afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is all closed up;
et cout la plaie.	and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	This head sticks in the intestine, and brings no harm to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a subtle thread that is cut from the intestine of a beast, in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the head of this thread of intestine that is very clean, and then tie to the head of this thread the thread of flax subtle twisted, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and put it back into the gut;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of treatment of fevers is not outside of the path of confidence and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and large, especially when it is in one of the intestinal gravel, if there is no ingen or health, then comes subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whichever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Be aware that every wound or abscess, when it suppurates, is called universally "fistula", and especially when it is hollow and has a cavity.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the true notion a false and hard and white node, where one does not feel pain, and is as hollow as the bone of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in a clear and hollow place, and other times in a thick one;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and it has no cartilage, this is not except by one of the VIII causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	it is to know, through the smallness of the wound or the body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its malice;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because it has hard cartilage within and on the lips, which does not allow cartilage to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or it has too much bone;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the limbs are rotten, and the material is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region has slow digestion, and slow healing, and is weakened by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or it has veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the symptoms, and the treatments of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is suitable that I make you know the treatment of fistula which is made by work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula has occurred in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and to the arteries, and to the kidneys, or to the diaphragm, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it happens that it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are of grievous affliction, and there is no lack of labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if it has any fistula that does not come near the place I have spoken of, and you have confidence in the cure, and you consider it, take a probe of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, if it seeks;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is twisted, seek it with a subtle probe of lead, because the leads bend easily around the twist;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot well search it with probes, then cleanse it through one of the openings, for the mucus flows from one opening to another, and purifies;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then feel it gently with your finger, to see if there is bone or nerve, and if it is excavated in the depth, and ask the patient well about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and the place where they feel it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the faulty and corrupted flesh that is within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the cure as long as it is healthy, and if the fistula is well perforated straight through, then you must cut deeply as much as you can, then put moist tents with sharp medicine, and push them just to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluous flesh that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put oil on healthy skin, as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healthy by that, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or sinew does not hinder or harm the principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove it as long as the corruption is entirely removed, then treat the things that are gangrenous until it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healthy, and an abscess bursts as before, know that you are not near a cure:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if it becomes uncovered and seek as long as you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the limb;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healthy, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this is not so, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot reach it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to let nature take its course;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can draw it out with forceps, use an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, draw them out one by one, do not leave any behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear, then cauterize and moisten and heat, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, then put on the wound a warm poultice, and let it stay until the limbs are rotten around the bones, and then they will be easier to extract the bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it's a large bone, such as the thigh or leg, then raise only the rotten part until the blackness is all bony, then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the corruption, and it comes just to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it is necessary to cut and scoop out all the way to the corrupted part, and then treat it until it is clean;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man around thirty years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from inside the body, so that the humors came to the leg, and it became inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no need to open it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the doctors in their foolishness opened it so much that the abscess burst open, and a lot of humors flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many openings came that discharged both bowel and body moisture;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many doctors treated the cure for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, so that I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what flowed out through the openings from his body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man became red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I touched a tendon in one of these perforations, and then searched all the perforations, and found that one vein came against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I then hastened, and cut into one of the perforations as long as I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came just to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I cleaned that which appeared to me of the corrupted bone, and believed that there was no other corruption, except for that which I had removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to treat the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and could not suture;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then began again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and cleaned it, and then removed it, and prepared to suture the wound;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I did not touch the inner part of the bone with my hand, and I pulled it back with all its mass, then I restored it with medicines;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it was healed and repaired quickly, and no longer needed to interrupt the work because of the weakness of the patient, who could not suffer, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For by the evacuation of blood often, but it was entirely healed, and a hard crust formed on the bone, and was of good disposition and had no nuisance nor discomfort from all of it, neither to eat nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, then it should be treated in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take the bandage, and hold the head of the bone that is dislocated, and instruct him to stretch it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another bandage on the thigh thicker than the first one, and tie it above the bone that is outside the hip, and stretch the skin, so that you draw the corrupt flesh to the lower part, and discover the flesh on the limb where you see the sore, so that the sore does not touch the flesh;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a piece of cloth or a pad behind the bone to support the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to show as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and sometimes even more.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the entire flesh;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then put a cloth behind, and then show from one part to the other the corruption, and let the surgeon be guided by the length of the corruption, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and be the bone or it contains from the other part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the connection of the two joints, then do not cut except for the part that is gangrenous;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the knuckle of the hand, or in the knuckle of the foot, it is a very strong thing, but nevertheless it is necessary that you inquire into this corrosion, as it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in all the ways that you can, but so that the vein or the nerve do not make a counter condition;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the cutting and the bones to be cut are many, according to the size of the bones and the appearance of the bones, and their thickness and thinness, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare each instrument for its similar work;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and be aware that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you prepare the instrument that you need according to what is necessary for it.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head may dislocate either from an internal cause or from a cause of heat;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have treated that corrosion with the cure of medicines, and they do not profit, then it is necessary to amputate that member up to where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes either from death or from evil, which is greater, the defect of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the members become black, as if they were burned by fire, and after the blackness, there comes a corruption of member into member, and it takes over the whole body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you hasten to the copper, and it is due to the percussion of certain venomous beasts, such as the sea scorpion and viper and similar things, if the corrosion is at the head of the pain, then anoint the copper, and do not give space for coming near the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes near the hand, anoint the copper at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it reaches the arm, anoint the copper on the elbow;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy stronger than the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do this for everything when the corrosion reaches the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it reaches the first joint, anoint the copper after the next joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it reaches the foot, anoint the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises to the knee, then cut at the joint of the kneecap.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes from above the knee, then there is no other remedy except to leave the patient to death;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the manner of cutting or of sawing the member is that you tie it above and below, and stretch one of your servants with the lower limb, and another servant with the upper limb, and you cut the flesh which is between the two limbs to a spatula wide, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or saw, and put on each part a dressing of linen, so that the saw does not touch the healthy flesh, and comes to the patient another injury and a new abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if a flow of blood comes when you make an incision, then cauterize the flesh immediately, or apply some powders that restrain.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine until it is accomplished, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healthy;
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to the man in his dream:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	a blackness appeared to him which seemed to be a burning of fire, and this corruption first came into his right foot, until it had taken over the whole foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he quickly amputated the foot, and was cured;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long time after, the corruption returned to the right hand, and he came to me, and I applied to him things that push back after the purification of the body, and I could not stop the corroisons;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to amputate his hand, but I refused, because I had hope of pushing back the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I doubted that if I cut his arm, he would not die, for the virtues of the man were weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he despaired of that, and returned to his land, and hastened to cure his arm, and was healthy;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not seen it told elsewhere that because of this one should make another part, which is in the craft.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes to the flesh and stays for so long that it makes a large gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then breaks and bursts, and out comes the pus, and stays in the body useless, like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is detached is as thin as a delicate cloth, and does not touch the bone, nor the nerve, and such an illness is called "sain", and not called "fistule";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so prolonged that it comes right up to the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you must cut around the whole wound, and likewise when it is subtle, like a delicate cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you think that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a cluster:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	look if the sins are large, and the belly that is in it is of foul odor, then administer the cluster of Egyptian medicine which is thus made:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take aquillity, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put the wound in a vessel over the fire, until the medicine becomes red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take from the seat according to necessity, and make it in a strait and in the middle, and narrow the body, and hold the buttocks;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine be in for 2 hours, then strain while squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breasts are reduced, and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and sometimes the straining is of narrowness from ashes, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes of the trunk of a vine, and throw narrow ones above, then filter, and strain, until you know that the breasts are well reduced;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot suffer it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the narrowness of ashes, then strain with narrowness and middle where it has a little bit of powdered litharge;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	You anoint with honey and mixed wine, that the honey has properties of purifying and washing, and the wine makes the blood rise.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you have ascertained that the blood is well purified, then you anoint with what creates birth of flesh in it, and you take a plaster made with definite gum, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you anoint it with certain medicines and oils, of which I have spoken the properties or treatment of the oils;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the hole in the breast is small, and the cane of the instrument cannot enter, then enlarge it a little with a metal file, and put on it a string of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too large, then sew and leave only as much of it open as the instrument can enter, and if the hole that the bowel is in is above or below where it should be.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is in the depths, do not let it protrude outside;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cover the belly as you wish, then prepare it in such a way that the bowel runs to the lowest place it is, for when the bowel is deep, do not let it protrude outside and if you cannot cover the belly as you wish, then prepare it in such a manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the bowel may run lightly downward, and do not leave anything of the bowel;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and apply a linen cloth that covers the entire wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cover the forces of the wound on the right side of the belly a little larger than before, then apply ointment softly on another cloth according to the quantity of the wound, and put it on the wound of the belly to alleviate it, and do not remove the large cloth outside except after many days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and he who is above the navel of the back, often breaks to break the bowel, and knows what comes from the bowel, if it is venom or poison or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take warning if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine is extended in such a manner and you see the nature that moves above the navel of the back, then know that the sins are open, and approach the sinews;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then loosen it in the morning, or the third day, and when you loosen the wound, if you change the other dressing, and renew the application of oil.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the sins evacuate undigested bowel after many days, know that the sins do not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut after long tension, do not despair of the health, for the sinews approach.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men whose tardiness in applying remedies to their wounds, and of those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if his navel is indigestible salt after many days, it knows that the breasts are not in agreement;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breasts are slow to agree, and it is prolonged, then we add dry medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diafinit ointment, for there is a large part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diafinit ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the extract of old wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then prepare the conserve and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and this same mixture makes a sweet cooked unguent, when diafinit ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then apply a plaster, and spread it on the breast, and sometimes administer to them a long aristologist, and roots of celestial herbs, which is as fine as flour of vetches and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in the use of simple or compound medicines:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them, and make into powder, and put on the honey that I mentioned, and use;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the treatment is prolonged, and it is not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption is deep-seated, and makes an impression on the bone, or on the hard members, or on the limbs;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if it is a matter of treating a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess on the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Painful swelling is an abscess that arises beneath the fingernail of the hand, or of the foot, or by accident arises in other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is inflamed, and no care is taken, then an abscess comes, and a painful swelling that grows as much as it grows to the root of the finger, and by chance it corrupts the whole;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and there comes corrosion to the bone, as far as there is foul-smelling pain, and the head of the sore is wide, and the color is dark brown.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not profit at all, then it is necessary that you cut with iron all the excess flesh that remains of the finger, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cautery is great aid if the bone is healthy and the fingernail is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the fingernail presses on the flesh and causes discomfort, and swelling, then it is necessary that you put under the fingernail a pointy instrument that touches the flesh, and push upwards, and cut the flesh subtly and lightly, and apply to the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the joints as long as they are healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, chop it off, and apply force, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the decay spreading, cut it off in the same way as it was said before, then heal it as long as it is healthy;
