Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you treat the wound on the foot, beware of the tendons that are underneath, and the tendon which passes across as in a joint.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flames be anesthetized.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot issue out, put the foot in a sling, and let the vein be well emptied.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the first dressing fails, recommend the second at a distance of a little, because the limb is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus make of the shin of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The limb of the sciatic vein is at the shins of the thigh, and its dressing is worth the pain of the hip, when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his urine is such that the patient urinates between the thighs, and strains upwards from the shinbone four fingers in turning, for otherwise the vein does not appear;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it appears, then urinate in all the ways that you can, and while passing through;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you take it, for the limbs are sound, and it is much put into the hands of men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not believe it, then urinate from the vein that appears on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make an issue of blood as much as you see, and then untie the ligature, and put on cotton and extract;
ele est maintenant sanee.	he is now bled.
des sainies de ventouse	of bloody discharges of the belly
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Discharges are made from horns, or from arsenic, or from pitch;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and ventilation is done according to two methods:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by striking and extracting blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this ventilation that is without striking is according to two methods:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is with all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and ventilation that is done by striking and by extraction of blood is done in thirteen places of the body, of which one is all on the summit of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others in the two sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the ventilation under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the ventilation of the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the ventilation on the knees;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the ventilations in the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the ventilations of the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the fat of the two cheeks;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the fatty tissue does not release any blood, for it is from the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason one does not become weak, as one does with the bleeding of a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that it be administered, nor to apply heat or cold, in any disease that comes from excess, as long as the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to apply fatty tissue, or through habit, then let us administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle and in every tension;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they have need to apply fatty tissue, then have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are some who experience excess and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness of the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such as spit a mouthful of blood, and have their tongue swollen, and vomit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if it is one of those who dream, and see in their sleep blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we command to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The blood of the nose helps the grief of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that it be after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this bleeding is in the place of the blood of the head, and it is not necessary that it be for one who is of a cold complexion or who has diarrhea, because these things cause them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it is not necessary for the old men to use it, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who often bleeds himself, becomes oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to put the cupping glass a little lower due to the doubt of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Cupping on the neck is in place of the bleeding from the head and of the basilic vein, and for this reason it is useful for the constriction of the lung, and for the fissure of the chest of the pormon, and for the cough, and for repletion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to bind little, because if it holds too firmly, it causes oblivion or stomach and heart problems.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	Cupping on the two sides of the neck is useful for head pains, and eye problems and migraines, and for strangulation, and for toothache, and it is in place of bleeding from the basilic vein.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is necessary that you instruct the bloodletter to press his hand on the spot, that he not cut the artery, and not cause a flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The evacuations of the mouth are good for diseases of the mouth, and for corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in the healing of the sores of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The evacuations of the shoulders are good for a disease that comes from heat and from fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The evacuations of the elbows are as good as those of the three veins of the arm, for it attracts blood from these thick veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the bloodletter not to make too deep an incision, for the limb is near to the flesh, and has many nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The evacuation that is on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for similar diseases, and it is necessary that the evacuation be large, and be of copper, so that it has the ability to treat well;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by accident, if it was fragile, it would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The ulcers of the legs heal openly, for they attract blood from the whole body, and are worth the old pains of the kidneys, and of the liver, and of the bladder, and bring back the flesh;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are in place of two hips, and of two knees, and completely weaken the body after long use, and bring about paleness in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply the ulcer treatment is that you put it first on the wound, and suck moderately, and put it firmly, and rub equally, and do not stop doing this, until you see the place red and swollen, and appearing with the redness of blood;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then do it, and put back the ulcers, and take warning in the condition of the body, for there are some who have such hot blood, and clear pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	If it is necessary to cauterize only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep;
et suce legierement.	and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the wound is large, then it is necessary to cauterize twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to subtily the passage of thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the wound is very thick, then it is necessary to cauterize a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to extract a little blood and a little, then we are sufficient with only one time.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, then we repeat often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the wound is thick, then cauterize deeply, and terminate it only when the blood flow seems to be stopped suddenly, and it is necessary for one who has thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the limbs with oil of saxifraga and dissolving;
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	It is an ointment made from violet oil, or from oil of sweet almonds, or from oil of cucumber seed.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and it is in ivy, made from oil of cresson, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other similar things.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is thick and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsam, or oil of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the skin is tender and has large pores, it is not necessary to apply any oil, but it is necessary to wash it after the application of warm rose water, or cold water, or water of mallow, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for one who has a lot of moisture, raise it with aqua vitae, or water of myrtle, and sumach, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities rise with old wine, or with water of sew, or with a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not suitable to apply a poultice of warm water before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for one or two hours;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is not suitable to sleep after the poulticing, and it is necessary that he be warmed, when he must be poulticed and when he is poulticed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And let those who are bilious beware, and if their blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is necessary that they take cold things, such as pomgranates and endives and lettuce to the stool, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and a little fat, and flesh of capon, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, should take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine moderately, which is between old and new, and little nuts, and little pork and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the more he is windy, the more he should drink than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is good to give to some men sometimes triaicle or nutmeg before or after the flatulence, to comfort the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be subtle, but it is not good that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The flatulence that is put without piercing are those that are put on the liver, and on the spleen, and on the podagre, and on the belly and the navel and the loins and the thigh, for these members do not suffer from being pierced with a needle, and one does not make them bleed except to attract blood from member to member, as we put on the mameles when there is an excess of blood;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To treat the viscosity which is in the limb, as we apply poultices on the belly and on the thigh to alleviate the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is an obstruction or stone, so remove by its attractive power through adventure the obstruction, or empty the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and let it be done when one applies it to the liver and to the spleen when there is retained viscosity, and these poultices are administered empty to suck as much as possible;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered together with cautery fire, and sometimes plain or mixed with hot water, as in cases of pleurisy illness, and in such manner that one fills the poultice with warm water, or with water in which one has cooked suitable herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the poultice administered to fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two fingers in width and half a palm in depth, and it has or costs on the inside of the middle a small perforation, just as if to push a needle, and let it be from the back so that it does not hurt the patient when putting it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and it has in the middle a rod of crossing made of iron or steel, to put a clamp on, and they are both large and small according to the illnesses and the expertise of those who use them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the veins of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin from those of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must then put this vein on the limb;
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	taking the clamp of wax or the plaster, and putting it in the vein across the rod that is in the vein, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the vein so it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and let your fingers be on the orifice that we have mentioned, so that when one wants, if the vapor goes in, and remove the ventouse;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the lining as before, and recommend it often, if you have mastery.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the ventouse then which is administered in disease of the pleura, to any sharp thing, it has no edge or orifice, and is not administered unless when it is full of water, and is put on the member as gently;
et c’est li forme:	and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Without them being administered unless on members where one cannot put ventouses due to their smallness, such as lips and cheeks, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the bare flesh of the body, such as fingers or knees, and other similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of urine is such that when you find sweet and clear urines which are in narrow passages, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in a narrow sweet tube, as long as they are familiar with it, and have nothing in their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be cured of vein and intestine, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and put on the urines;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are flat, and will discharge, if it is a good place or where one can put intestine, then put it, for it is worth much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the place of the haunch, and then of the passage, very well, and then squeeze it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the places are too sore afterwards near the body of the urines, then wet a linen cloth in cold passage, and put on, until the urines are constricted;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if his blood is multiple, then put on a warm broth, or galen, and similar things, until it is stretched;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the limb moistened warm fava beans, and let them be until they adhere to the limb, it will now stretch;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you are in a state of greater expertise, then take other bloodlettings.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the bloodlettings do not want to take, then rub the limb with fresh blood, or you stick an needle in as long as the blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they adhere;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they cling, then powder on a bit of aloe and of dried and ground cinder, or of ash, and they will now adhere.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish people reject this chapter, for they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor have they learned from letters;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the science is foreign in our land, because I have never found any good there;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing, except that by the science of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are needed, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we say in the prologue of this book the sum of the word and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsions or concussion comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to anoint the patient on one side and the other, unless something prevents you from doing so, as weakness of the body, or infants, or old people.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if it is not too hot for him, nor too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and avoid cold and chilled foods, that is to say cold joints, and meat of goat and of pork, and do not drink wine, and avoid fatty and greasy foods, and do not fill oneself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you are no longer in doubt about a hot abscess, or an accumulation of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient returns to their previous governance, he will have used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to mend, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with foods that promote fat gain, or have viscosity, such as cooked broth in water, and pork, and testicles, and feet, and calf liver, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a warm nourishment will repair bones and will be very beneficial for the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the elderly and decrepit cannot well mend or reunite according to their nature due to the dryness of the members, nor those which are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but in order to heal, reset the bone that is broken and tie the large tendons which hold the member together, until it becomes strong as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and not the whole point of his work, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish him with thick foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And be aware that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that come from a blow, and another from a fall, such as the cut of a quill pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with only a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own technique, and its proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory recalls in its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the fracture of the bone is by what the joints are twisted, and apparent through swelling, and heard when pressing with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when it does not have twisting in its touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no point of fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary that you move the limb, but put on medicines that come to it afterwards, and then strain it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture which comes from a blow, and are the two parts disjoined, it is necessary now to put them in place equally, just as abscesses of the foot come to life;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if a hot abscess comes, then let it be until the abscess is appeased, without leaving any pus, as long as the abscess is calm;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it equally in the place where you can set it lightly and wisely, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restorations of a skull or where it has pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then he tightens, as it is necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if it breaks into pieces in the bones, depending on whether it's the hands or feet, or to your hand if it's small members, or to the tendons, or to one tendon and to your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are reduced, reset by all means the additions in their places at the joint that you can, and beware that through your work there comes to the patient no injury or pain;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two ends of the bones according to their proper forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with the hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if the dressing is gentle, and not tightening too much, nor pressing as those do who make it come through their work abscess heat and contraction to the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is at stake, instruct the patient well that they should not move it, neither while awake nor while asleep, nor while turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the limb is so secured that it doesn't feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, then it is not at stake, and it is necessary to put it in such a position that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is placed straight, so that twisting does not come when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in smallness and in largeness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small members, such as arms and fingers and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	it is necessary to envelop them with soft and subtle bandages;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those which are thick, such as the thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	if it is necessary to envelop with a large and hard linen bandage, because the wide bandages press the entire large member, and constrict all sides equally, so that there is no unevenness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then wrap lightly three or four turns according to the member, and constrict the hand a little on the entire bandage, then go above the fracture and constrict less, than the fracture, then loosen a little the fracture;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the bandage a little and often, as much as you press a large portion of the healthy limb, then take another bandage, and turn around again above the fractured limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the fracture, and constrict moderately, neither too strongly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first bandage above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the lips of the wound a swab of linen or cloth, as long as it is even and equal, then tie everything with a bandage above, and then put your dressings well made on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then put on a thing that appeases the abscess with heat, and which removes the swelling, and leaves it thus for some time;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then strain on your dressings, and let them be of the humor of a large, wisely cut, cainne, or of the wood from which one makes the clubs, or of the roots of palm, and let them be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the dressing one puts on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and let it be as long as it is necessary for the size of the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then hold it steady on the stelae as you did in the first lesson, then tie above a vein similarly as in the first lesson on the bruising.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	The narrower it is tied above, all the less;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, not too thick nor too thin, and be of soft flax;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the work of foolish people who make their ligatures with twisted flax cords, and it is a great error, because the ligature cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it is not necessary that it has between each steel less than two fingers of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is annoyed by the sides of the stelae after the constriction on their sound limbs, then put on them a bandage of flax or a piece of linen cloth, so that it does not chafe.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the chest is broken, I will tell you about the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And be aware that it's not necessary to strain these bones when all the fractured limbs are first broken.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it's not necessary to put these [bones] in place until after 5 or 7 days, or more according to the severity of the abscess and the swelling that occurs;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and know this is the manner of the ancient plasterers for restoring fractures, dislocations, and sprains:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take the flour that holds at Paris from the mill, and mix it with warm water, and put this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the plasterer restoring the fracture in many ways, and likewise for women and for small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of plaster for restoring the fracture and the dislocation and the sprain:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take barberry and lasmine and enula and asafoetida and Arabic gum and moguet, an ounce or so;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloe, an ounce and a half;
alechil VIIII З.;	of alichol eight ounces;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make into powder, and mix with oil of beef;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the temperament of the man is cold, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores the broken bones quickly, and is of benefit to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of plaster that is good for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take moguet and vismalve, an ounce or so;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloe, eight ounces;
acaice VI З.;	of acacia six ounces;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Boil armenic, and bruise well, and mix with water or wine of vinegar, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to plaster the joints and the bones dislocated from their places, and appease the sudden pain, and the cut of the bone, and the bruising:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take a new wool, and anvil in oil and cooked, and put on the body.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore, but they are good for appeasing hot abscesses, and properly relieving the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to plaster that restores the broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves, and earthy roots of plantain, and bruise them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to plaster for the restoration of the bone fracture and to calm the irritation of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of violets, camomile, flowers of violets, flour of peas, of each one part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and pound, and mix with wine, and if the limbs are swollen, mix it with water of moist coriander or with water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another kind of plaster stronger than the first, when hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of violet, and seeds of flax, balaust, melilot, and sage, and flowers of violets and of camomile, of all one part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and pound, and mix with water of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on a broken limb for restoration of force except the paste made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and says it should be between two, not too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems reasonable to apply to the broken member warm and slightly hot things, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way of applying a plaster that is good for an injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mugwort and roots of decapitated homes, or feathers of birds, and wormwood, and equal quantities, and pound them, and make a plaster with the glue.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then undo it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor is the bone of their body injured;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if it does not come undone by itself.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain or itching comes to the body, without rest or relief, then hasten, and undo it, and remove the plaster at once;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And take a light cloth, and a sea sponge moistened, and plunge it in water, and lift it up to the limb, until the itching stops, and the pain is alleviated.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply to it a dry, or moistened in water or rose oil, linen cloth, and tie it with a nut, until you are sure of the aposteme's heat;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and reduce the inflammation of the limb, and let the pain be eased, then apply a subtle plaster, and a little poultice, and do not constrain it as strongly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it gently until it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the aposteme, heat and redness and pain and swelling are gone from everything, and you have need of poultice and of linen cloth, then apply it again, as you did previously in the same way.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if it does not come to the limb any of what we have said, do not force the dislocation for three or four or five or seven days;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes let it be twenty days, according to what one sees, until the fracture becomes solid, and approaches the adjustment of the flesh together;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then restrain it more than at first, and bind its vein, as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the limb drying out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come to it;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	raise then the cold and wet dressing, every time that you dislocate it, and let this be on the third day, and loosen a little the ligature;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this work then cut the nourishment to the limb, and amend immediately what foolish doctors do, who torture the member excessively:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is harmful, and such practices are to be feared, and I do not see anything other than giving pain and making things worse.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of fractures exist, and there are various shapes, and the causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures made by the blow of a sword, and the bone is broken all the way to the joint that is next to the surface of the bone, as if done with an axe or club;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "axing" or "hewing".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	When the sword cuts the bone with a blow from below, and it is called this kind of fracture "absolue" or "cutting from underneath";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and the wound from these two fractures is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has been struck with a blunt object, or cracked, or broken from a fall on stone, or fallen on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing wound, which approaches just to the web that is beneath the bone, or it is on the bone, and this is a wound whether large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that has grown into the bone as subtle as a goat's hair, and the fissure is small, and for this reason it is called this fracture "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or a similar thing, and it causes the piece of bone to enter inward, and the limbs are twisted as the blacksmiths do when they strike on the anvils;
si entre li piere dedens.	if between the inner bones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have soft or moist bones, such as a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these manners of fracture that small pieces are dislocated thus;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak of its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures through the extraction from them, and the questioning with tents, and by the corrupted flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The resemblance of hair is known by that which when one discovers the bone, and one rubs upon it, then appears the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of the fracture, beware of accidents by the patient, and if you see any evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and tension, and palpitations, and acute fever, and the eyes bulging out and reddening, and other similar things in many dispositions, cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a terrifying accident, and you expect health, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the injury comes first to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to uncover the bone before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the bone tissue does not become corrupted, and comes the accident that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you suture the affected part thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and it is that you take the head of the afflicted patient, and uncover the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound as gently as you can, and if a decrease of blood comes to uncover the bone, or a abscess falls, use what aid is necessary, and it is that you fill the hole with moistened cloths soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the fallen abscess is appeased, and be assured of a decrease of blood;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then it begins between the bone and the flesh, and it is done according to two manners of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One manner is that you cut at the narrow tail end in front, and that is its shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then you widen the other end, making it larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is that you have a number of diverse ends, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are made of iron;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and in working lightly, so that you do not harm the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce through, in such a way that you administer ends with grooves, not so that they penetrate beyond the bone of the head, and must have on the end a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and it is necessary to have several, so that each one comes into his own place in the hope of the bones, so that you have supporters for all tests;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three manners of supporters:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing through the broken bone is that you put one supporter on the bone, and turn with your hands as long as you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then put the supporter on another part a little afterwards, and thus do all around, then cut with incisions the space of the bone which is between the parts, and do this more subtly than you can, and gently, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have, such as tongs, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and beware that you do not touch the brain nor the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone, and drawn, it is necessary that you restore the part that has remained of the bone to all other similar instruments resembling an incisor, but it is necessary that it be more delicate and more subtle than the other incisors;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if there remains nothing of the small bones, or any shells, then lightly touch the bones to one of the instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with tenderness and caresses that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another manner of work is what the Gauls call, which is more familiar;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and it holds very strongly, and this is its effect.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you discover a part of the bone, whether it be broken or bruised, so that when you have discovered that part, then you will put at the head of this instrument, which is called a lenticle, whose form is this:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut on one side, and the affected part is in two edges, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then make with a small hammer above, so that you gently cut the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane that is beneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is close to the bone, gently cut the bone, for one cuts well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not reach to the membrane, and the bone is cut just above, and it has small pieces, then it is necessary to render that asperity, and to remove the scales with a subtle rasp that you must have in different quantities, to apply to each place the most convenient, according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Use coarse rasps at first, and afterwards finer ones, and do not stop from doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other fine haircuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you make adjustments according to its thickness.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and it is something that is not prescribed for one who has devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is deep, then you must take a cloth of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and put it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another double cloth, in two or three layers, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as gently as you can, so that you do not irritate the wound, then apply another linen cloth on top, and do not bind it too tightly, just enough to touch the wound;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it be thus for one or two days, until the aposteme abscess is appeased, then undo it, and apply medicines such as roots of lily, and flour of vetches, and powder of incense, and aristolochia, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and of these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer at the same time medicines without mordication;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and guard that the wound is immediately clean, so you do not leave in it the pus, nor leave to gather filth, for when filth gathers on the cloth of the brain, it corrupts and festers, and brings great evil to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one puts on the affected part a cauterizing thing, it becomes worse through neglect.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, that no evil accident comes to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come forth for the medicine that one has put on, which has virtue, then it is necessary that you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue one drag, and put it on the affected place;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then for the treatment of manners of cures that are suitable, as long as he is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	It is known that sometimes both parts of the knee joint are broken, or one of them alone, because they are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and this cartilage is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it becomes swollen or twisted, and then becomes diseased.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is necessary that you bind your little bandage or splint around the knee, and put equal to this break inside your bandage index, and in the pouchet by default, until the knee regains its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it lightly, and guard that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the knee, and the bone cannot come to its place, then it is necessary that you put it even at the head of a stick somewhat thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, thus make another, and hasten to restore the first joint, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscessed place is cooled, then apply to the head of the fracture a poultice made with bandages of linen, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you apply to the other part, where the fracture is;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the openings of the fracture.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some say one should moisten the bandages in butter, and change every joint.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is good, but rather that they should be moistened with a concoction of egg and powder of mallow;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the bandage on, until the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes the button of an abscess is opened with a needle, and if it is loosely wrapped in a bandage, and the fracture is held, and the patient breathes through.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	For do that which you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the urine as you urinate, then put a little cotton moistened with rose oil, or in a pouch of hyssop.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscesses do not come, then apply a plaster made from flour of cypress, and powder of incense, mixed with water, then put on light poultices, and do not tie around the kidneys.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the fracture of the kidney is small, and it is broken into tiny pieces, then extract the excrements suitable for that, then sew the wound, and treat the things that cause inflammation and swelling, as with plasters and ointments suitable for that.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it has no deep wounds, then the treatment of tents, and he puts bandages of plaster, as long as it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken apart, and there is no point of the wound to be found, and the breaking is only slightly so, and it is not broken in two, unless the bone is corroded within, then one examines it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the breakage is on the right side, that you put your right index finger in the mouth of the patient;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the breakage is on the left jaw, then put your right index finger, and gently push the breakage from within, and hold the other side with the other hand from outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the breakage of the jaw is separated in two, then it is necessary that you administer extension to the two parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the teeth are shaken by a rupture, or a fracture, then hold them back with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken jaw a kerchief, and put on the dressing twice;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and put on the dressing a large staple well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it around the mouth that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the fracture is changing, then untie it on the third day, and then put back in place what has changed;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a plaster on it, made from powder of millstone with egg white or flour of oats, after you have applied the kerchief;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put on a light linen plaster, and if the plasters stick, and the condition of the patient does not change, let it be until it is healed;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times it is healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses that come, then we will treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if it has a fracture and wound together, restore the nude piece of bone in being bone;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if subtlety of the bone the extracted fragments reunite with that.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with a flame according to necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have bones all these pieces, and none remain, then sew the wound, if it is large, and put on it some plasters united to that, to bind flesh, until it be healthy.
de la forcele	of the fracture
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The fracture breaks many times before, towards the shoulder, and the break is in three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	Or when it is broken and dislocated in two places, and there are fragments, and it is more difficult to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or where there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is such that when the break is without a wound, you should have two attendants, so that one holds the injured area where the break has occurred;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other stretches the neck towards the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then put the break equally between your two hands, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor deviation.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend it further, then put on the shoulder of the patient a round sphere made of cloth, or of wool, and let its size be according to your necessity;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and stretch and lift the injured area, and hold the sphere in your hand, so that you put the break in its proper place;
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder out of its joint, because it comes from deep within, then it is necessary that the patient put his hand on his hip, and place the middle of the shoulder on the tip of the elbow, and turn the lower end of the shoulder downwards, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then take the fracture in your hands, and if you pull it straight, it is necessary that you cut into;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and pull the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any swelling, then cut according to one of the incisions that you have;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but that you put on the shoulder this instrument, to guard the skin:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and resembles a spoon, and is not too narrow, and should be as wide as it is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the thickness of the tissue;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it has two parts, as you see, and let one be large, and the other be narrow, just as is the condition of the wound that you have made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are assured of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the condition is small, or you doubt the abscess is hot, then fill the wound with dressings and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, then moisten the dressing in oil and rose water and vinegar, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The strengthening of the bone, when it is without wounds and without surgery, is that you apply to the bone a plaster made from powdered mallow and egg white, and apply light bandages, and put a splint under the dressing, if you have the skill;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide bandage of a palm's length, then put a double cloth on the swelling, and apply the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a thin stick of three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around the bandage, so that one end of the bandage hangs down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and put the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage around the neck, and undo the healthy shoulder, and undo the diseased shoulder;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset each part, and when you see that the ligaments hold the fracture firmly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move on the broken bone, then check every day, and when the ligaments are relaxed, then restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put when he sleeps a small pillow under the shoulder, to raise the joint upwards.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If the fracture of the upper arm is reduced by the reduction of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and no bad accident happens, until twenty days;
