puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then reapply the plaster, if you see that it is needed, and hold it in place and let it be, until it is restored;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is most often restored in twenty-eight days, and in less than eight weeks.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It happens that the broken or dislocated shoulder does not heal in the middle, and it is not felt to be out of place except by the touching;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if the bandage conforms to the shape of the fracture, and the dressing conforms to its natural form, in all the ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on the wound powder of millet with a little water, and light dressings, and put over it a double bandage;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then put on a wide and thin stake, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the stake is dislocated it moves in no place of the shoulder, unless one uses a poultice of hot linen, so that the stake becomes straightened;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then bind it all with a large bandage firmly, so that the stake does not move from its place, and look at the linen every day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and every time it becomes dislocated, bind it, and put the stake straight as it was out of its place, and let the patient lie on their side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or in 25.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number of days is accomplished, then untie it, and be careful, for it is not good to keep it tied too long.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes forward, and pushes against the heart, then make an incision, and the oste, and do what we have said in the breaking of a false abscess of hot aposteme.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The feet are sometimes fractured in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it breaks often at the toe
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is fractured in the middle, it declines to the toe, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and weakness, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the bowel in the broken bone, and loses his senses.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient often places on his back, and puts a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the sides of the two ribs with his hands, and subtly adjusts to make it even in all ways that you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then put on plasters and stoppings above the subtle splint of salt, or another light paste, and wrap it in a bandage, and tie it to the broken bone, so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the linen bandage around the back, and tighten it firmly, and rewind each hour the bandage, and if it becomes loose, then tighten it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it becomes necessary to loosen it, due to corrosion or itching that comes to the wound, or pain or abscess, then hasten and loosen it, and render the plaster, and address what has come from various methods of treatments;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reset the plaster, and tighten it as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	It is known that the fracture of the ribs does not come from a blow except when there are large blows on the back, and on the inner chest, and do not cause pain except because they are swollen;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and the pain is especially bad at the time of urination.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put even the fracture, as it is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and hold it with a stick, if you have this in your profession.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the fracture of the ribs declines inward, then the patient feels great pain and puncture, as with a case of pleurisy, for the bone pierces the membrane;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and sharp pains, and coughing and vomiting a great quantity of blood, and it is a grievous condition, and the old men have given much advice.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is one of those who say that it is necessary to administer foods which inflate the stomach, in order to push out the fracture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, because a hot abscess does not come, if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, thus let it be.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they say that none of the veins should be cut on the body to suck out the humor, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	Nevertheless, there is doubt that the veins do not attract the excess humors of the body due to the weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the body with a warm woolen cloth soaked in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to equalize the flow within, then it will be cured by the treatment of the cure of pleurisy, of diet and of medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear the pressure on the bone which points to the lung, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut into the body of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument inside to guard against the damage.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut the bone, and shave lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and apply a dressing to it, until it becomes healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if a carbuncle appears, put on it a moistened cloth soaked in rose oil, and apply it to the body;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the place from which it comes that gives rise to the carbuncle, and apply poultices to the affected area where it should be, until it becomes healthy.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a fracture comes to the bones of the neck, and it seems that it will break;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, take heed if you see their hands softened and swollen and deadened, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when one holds them firmly and tightly, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if one applies a cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, then take heed if the feet are swollen, and if the accidents that occur are in the hands, and on the back there is sweating and vomiting without desire;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one has it seated on their stomach, then there is vomiting without desire.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is seated on its back and it wants to sit, then it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if one does not work at his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to them, then the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you apply if there is a hot abscess, put on the spine oil of rose or oil of mallow's root, until it is appeased;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that side where he feels the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if some bone becomes dislocated, then it is necessary to sew over the heart;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and reduce the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat the joint with gum arabic, until he is healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the elbow", you thrust your fist into your left hand, and place it even with your other hand on your shoulder, then apply the plaster and set it straight, if you have skill;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then hold it back, and if there is a bone uncovered, make an incision above, and on the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the thigh
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It happens that the bone of the thigh is fractured, and if it happens, then there is not much help from a little manipulation at the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and it causes lengthwise pain, and decline to the patient, and comes to the sick person pain in the leg, and sharpness, and swells what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you put your hand on it, as long as you are above the fracture;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and you should know what the breakage and its shape are;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is at the head of the bone, then put equal to that fracture, as long as it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is of long duration, or it declines inwardly, then have the patient lie on their stomach, until the restoration of that break is apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have made it even, put on a plaster, then put on a splint of wood or of leather, and hold the break steady, so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and anoint the limb below the ribs, until the injury is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient that they should sleep on their sound side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if hot abscesses come, do not touch them, until the hot abscesses are alleviated, and put on what we have previously mentioned;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and hold it as is necessary, if there is no other bad accident;
et c’est li maniere.	and it is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The joints are what is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, thus one must restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take a wooden splint of moderate thickness, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two joints the two bands, and bend them upwards, and sit the patient on a seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then put the arm with the broken bone on the splint, until it comes to the elbow, and have in the middle a curve of wood, then tie above some heavy thing where the minister extends downwards;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then put the mire the fracture even with his hands together, so that the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that one binds the patient to his bed, and ties his hand to his neck, then instructs the servants that one of them takes what is on the bruise in his hands, and the others take below all the linen, and stretches each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forced, then hold the linen below the bruise and on the bruise, and stretch each of the servants to his part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the bruise is near the head of the shoulder, then it is necessary that you put one linen under the armpit, and the other towards the elbow, under the bruise.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the bruise is towards the elbow, then it is necessary to put the linen lightly, without pressure, until the bruise is even on the limb and on the elbow;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then put even the fracture, if it is necessary, and hold it steady, so that abscesses do not come to the wound.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses do come, then do not hold it tight for seven days, and put on a moist cloth and oil of roses, until the abscess is reduced.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then hold it steady, and the manner of holding is that you put a plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm with the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the back.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put on a bandage, and hold to the shoulder, and to the arm, so that the arm is in its place, if nothing can dislodge it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone will not move, then use splints, and put on the fracture a splint larger and stronger than the others, and let there be between each splint two fingers' space, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three fingers on each side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then strain on the stiles, thus as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, stronger and less in aligning.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the alignment of the stiles, and the constriction, as we have said, in the work that you restore the broken member, and you suspect hot abscess, let it be until the seventh day, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then examine each for three days the ligament, that swelling or inflammation does not come to the limb, or the nourishments cannot come to the member because it is too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it decreases, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accident comes, then do not force the dislocation further that after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and put his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put a dislocated shoulder in its proper place with a pillow of wool evenly, and watch each hour of the day or night, that the alignment of the member does not break nor the tendons become slack;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if it adheres by virtue of medicine, and give the food that we have previously mentioned, in such a manner that the food is first subtle;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to seize, then it should be coarse.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be seized for 40 days from everything;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must dislocate it and administer baths and medicines of anointings for the joint to adhere;
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the fracture is ugly and swollen, then it will take 40 days or 2 months to disentangle.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "radius" and "ulna", one of which is small, and it is the one that connects to the shoulder;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is the one that is twisted, towards the little elbow;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	by chance, the large radius bone will break alone, or the small one, and by chance they will mend together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small radius bone is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large one is broken, then the healing is bad, and more troublesome than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small radius bone that is broken alone, then it is necessary to set it lightly in place, and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the large radius bone, then it is necessary to set it with more force;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and stretch out on the cushion, and pull the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and let the little fingers be lower than the other fingers, and let the patient cross their arms over themselves, and the cushion in front of them higher, so the patient does not suffer any hardship;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then stretch out the ministers like arms to the part below his hand, or to the elbow, and one minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the mire equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is no matching piece to join the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make a splint and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the break there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter;
si pren la cure.	If you take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if at the beginning of the restoration there appear abscesses and swellings, apply a plaster made from oil and white wax, which should be neither too hard nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and spread the plaster subtly on it, until the abscesses and swellings are alleviated.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the wax, and apply a plaster made from powdered millstone with a little water, then put on the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be stronger, and a bit larger than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it must have six splints or arms in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	be it that the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and hold more firmly on the fracture than other parts, and all the less so in touching, as I said at the beginning of the chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and are the bandages that are on the fracture soft and moist, and not hard nor harsh;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread, from which it is strained, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And bind the limb and the thread after a few hours.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if some evil accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then it is necessary that you wrap the limb with warm water, until those itchings are alleviated;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb not be restrained from resting.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then restart the tightening, and if the threads are softened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, if it is necessary.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And beware that the numbness cannot come to the limb, because it is too tight, then it is necessary that you loosen it a little, and leave it thus for some hours, until the numbness departs, and then tighten.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not untie him for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or put a bandage around his neck, then bind his hands to his neck, and let his neck be even, and guard against movement and digestion, and let him sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and by chance in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and as we have said, there are few fractures, and it rarely comes to a point where there is often splinting.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or split, then it is necessary that the patient sit cross-legged, and sit upright in front of him evenly;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then he puts his hand on the extended leg, and extends the mangled bones, and puts the muscles even with the bones, as long as they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and applies a plaster and the poultices, if abscesses do not come, then he puts a splint according to the quantity of the defect;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is on the inner side of the sole of the foot, make a sphere of cloth, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken foot;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then bind it with a long cloth, and let the splint be of leather soft enough as the palm of the hand, and bind it, as is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the finger, it is necessary that you put a splint on top, and another below on the palm, so that the hand is straight and upright, then tie it all around the hand, and tighten the cloth between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture comes to one of the two bones, it is the forearm, set it straight, as it is necessary;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and restrain it with a splint, and if you see that a small straight stick is put to lift the fracture, and does not move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is in the other arm, as in the elbow or one of the others, set it straight, and bind it with the healthy arm that is next to it;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you tie them both together, so that they do not move, or you put a stick on, as on the forearm;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and in the treatment of hot abscesses, and heal those that come from it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see it well when it turns to the front and back;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is when one puts a bandage under the fracture, and another above it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient puts his face on it, then each assistant extends his hand to his part equally;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and it is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, one of the assistants should be at the groin, and the other assistant above the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, and then the assistant should be at the knee, and the extension should be below;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then put the bones equal with his two hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, if abscesses do not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it cool, then return to your work and to its treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The book is made in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you bind the fracture with a bandage doubled in two or three layers, and let the surplus hang over, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the knee, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and let the end of the thread come out above.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn the bandage on the leg and on the thigh, then put these on the fracture, and put a stake on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make equal pressure, then begin to bind firmly two or three turns around the fracture;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and the more you go up from the fracture, the less it is constricted;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then understand the two heads of the thread that you have placed between the thigh and the hip, and in their place there are three stitches that are detached, then return to the bottom at the head of the thread, until you come up near the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and hold it steady, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, and that there comes neither abscess nor swelling nor any similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens, then undo it, and treat what has come, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if it is a piece of bone that hurts, then make it grow, if one can;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, then make the place grow by cutting and scraping;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the hip is broken thus where one puts stitches, as in the shoulder and or arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	In all ways, during restoration thus made not ringing to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it is known that the thigh is restored in a day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of the complications.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the hollow of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is known that in the hollow of the knee there is little breaking, but it often swells.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is nothing but a fissure, or a perforation, and there is a complete wound, and without a wound, and that feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is when one puts even what is broken to its two parts, as long as they are assembled as one can.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then apply the plaster, and you put on a round bandage, if you have the skill, and hold it as is necessary, then examine all the treatments that we have said for other fractures, such as abscesses, heat, and similar things;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Put to each accident what is suitable for it, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Be aware that in the leg there are II bones, because of which one is called by right "tibia", and the other is called "fibula";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and it has the same kind of fracture as the arm, and for this reason the restoration is just like that of the arm, and the work is all the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg becomes twisted on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bone is broken, then it becomes twisted forwards.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, then one feels great pain, and the swelling is visible;
et torne desoz.	and it becomes deformed.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then we apply extension, and put it in place, and lay the splints equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but however, it is necessary if the fracture is ugly, and it has many pieces, that the extension be smaller and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and the wing according to its strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two pieces of split wood that press against the thigh on one side and the other, and are as long as the thigh from the knee to the buttocks;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap two splints with one bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle, and to this binding the thigh should not turn to the right or left, and thus it is well;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and let someone apply a splint as long as the thigh, and it is of wood, and put it on the thigh to prevent movement, and properly made for the fracture or where there is a wound;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each day the leg, to see if it has an abscess or another accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if you treat him as long as he is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	To the ankle comes no fracture, but to the bones of the foot come sometimes fractures and to the two knees, and it does not happen that they are shattered in many different ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is a fracture of the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, then put the patient's foot on the ground, just as if he were going to walk, and then put your foot on top of his, where the bones are raised, then press down until they return to their place;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then apply the plaster and bandages above, and put beneath the belly of the foot two flat splints, then bind it to the foot firmly, then you have enveloped the dressing around, and other things that you have need of.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if you untie the bandage, you will find the bones even, whether they are broken, whether they are dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are some of the fingers broken, restore them, as we have said about the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then put on the broken finger a splint according to the length of the finger, and let it be a little wider, then put next to the foot the tablet that I have spoken of, and bind it tightly;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken, put on each finger a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the tablet next to the foot;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let it be placed on top of the tablet across the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, since we have spoken of them.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each accident as it is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone in the thigh of the woman is fractured, if it makes her sit with enlargement, then bend her to the back part, and let it be held from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the bath with warmth of the patient's body heat, and put in it as much [water] as [the quantity that is] sufficient;
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then undress the woman, and raise her back a little by little, and then press the cloth, until it comes to the entrance of the thigh, and the bone returns with the rest;
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, remove the cloth, and when she has urinated, put it back on her, and do this for seven days or inside;
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	If it will be restored the fracture, and you see, take a bladder of goat, and tie to the fractured area a string, and pour all the bladder into the wound;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow in the string strongly, until the bladder is inflated from within:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the wound will then restore the fracture;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then it should be filled with cotton, and left thus for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the shoulder of man is broken, or of woman, thus it should be restored as we have said for the bone of the thigh;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these nearby fractures are not hidden from one who applies his study and work, and attends to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture signifies in many ways the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	pay attention then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	On the stick, when it is broken, take a handful of ivy and bind the stick;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap it with bandages around, and leave it for three days or therein, and it will be healthy soon.
de brisure avec plaie	of a fracture with a wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that it be healed now, so that the healings that we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then anoint with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then recommence to restore the fracture in the same hour, or that day, if abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is alleviated, and do not touch it on the third day nor on the fourth, for you will cause bad accidents to come.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the heart of the uncovered wound, then it is necessary that you put it in place lightly with your hands, with small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension is not prepared to be put in place by your hands, then reset it with this instrument made of iron, which has 7 or 8 fingers in length, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason it is necessary for the master that he take 3 or 4, according to what he needs in each treatment of a fracture;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and let it be rounded and somewhat thick, so that it does not press on the member during your work, and let it be pointed at the front, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palainche", because it is necessary that the curved head be put on the top of the exposed bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and strike it once, as long as it grows back, and let one be even with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the surgeon cannot well grasp the bone, then it is necessary that you cut off the end of the bone, so that the surgeon has possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, then cut it with an instrument suitable for that purpose, whether to cut or to scrape, according to your ability.
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	Then remove what remains in the bone of callus and small spurs.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	Do this until it is in its place, then wrap it in a bandage soaked in black styptic wine, and apply it neatly if it is in a splint.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put anything on the wound, such as cerote or other things that have oil, so that it does not cause suppuration and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer these once you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover it all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted with the dressing;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times foolish physicians have done this, and have caused death or corruption to come upon the patient;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the dressing be softer and more gentle than other dressings.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a serious accident may occur, as we have said, and you feel pain in the body, then it is not suitable to put these on;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap around, on the body of this dressing, a cloth, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days the wound beginning to fester, then remove what you had applied on top of everything, and put on a healing ointment for wounds, such as ointment called tetrapharmacum and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you unbind the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is sound and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be bound in such a way that the wound can flow downwards slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass, and it cannot heal but rather discharges continuously, know that there are small pieces of bone, because of which it is necessary that you touch the wound with a probe, and remove all these loose pieces that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula or other kind of corruption comes to the limb, then it is necessary that you treat it, according to what is written in its chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken, and open on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or of the shoulder, and other similar ones of the large limbs, do not touch it, because many times death comes from it, but let it be until it becomes calloused;
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	By chance it will close itself after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound, if you can;
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, then leave it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the bruises that come on the abscess
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We come many times after the health of the bruising, especially when it is near the joint, and the bad thing is to see the shape of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance it cannot make the limbs do their natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take care then that the nostrils are fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if you administer medicines that dry up, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and other similar things, so that you prepare one of these things, or all together, and mix them with wine that dries up or with absinthe or with vinegar;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and put them on the nutmeg in stops, and constrain it well, and do not untie it with gentle movements;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then reset it, and restart another one, until the swelling is reduced;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you constrain on a well-made piece of plaster;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of plaster is that it reduces all the swellings above the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the swelling is already converted into hardness like stone, and it is in need of being cut, then cut above it, and make the excess apparent;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you treat it with some ease, until it is reduced, and the treatment until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and it remains weak and subtle after the healing of the members, this happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	because one is for this that it was tied too tight, and was not tied as it was supposed to be
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because it had too many ties, and the nourishments could not come to the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or because of a multitude of swelling;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or because of too great movements, not in its time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because it has little blood in its body, so is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body tender, so that the blood is multiplied in him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and give it a bath, and give joy and happiness;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then put poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and the swelling of the hot water, until the nourishment runs to the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the member is twisted after the injury
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the members are twisted after the restoration, and the broken bones are exposed, and the form of the member is ugly, it does not lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	if one does not believe the fools who say that one should break the member anew, and many foolish doctors have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and these practices are to be blamed, and great evils come from them, and death often results;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	however, if the nodations and the swellings are fresh, then it is necessary that they be treated with warm water, or that softening herbs be applied, such as leaves of violette, and roots, and melilot, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and make a softening plaster, such as a well-made diacaluminum, and take the muscle of violette, and mix it with the fat of a goose or oil of cypress, and apply the plaster;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	Or you take fat figs, and crush them with cinnamon powder, and similar medicines that reduce the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is soothed by continually and for a long time rubbing with a moist hand.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And restore movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the tortured part is inflamed and hardened, like stone, and needs to be operated on with iron, then you should cautiously cut just to the bone, subtly and lightly;
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put caution and study into the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here is the translation of the sentence: Thus begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if you need to now bring back into alignment.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if it is delayed, the limbs become swollen, and by chance, one resets them to the right place;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	because it is not suitable to move it to the hole where it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times it causes spasms and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	in any case, when this happens, make the patient sane, then let him be, until the abscesses and ulcers are appeased;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the limb from the cold and oily water, then reset it gently, and treat each member as the treatment will come into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It happens that the jawbones are dislocated and loose, and the dislocation of both is in two ways:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	where they are a little loosened from their places, and softened a little;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	where they are entirely dislocated, and hang towards the pis, and cut the saliva from the mouth so it cannot be held, nor can the mouth be closed, and envelops the tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns due to the many arrangements of the body.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is entire and complete, then it is necessary that you reset it quickly, and do not tarry;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a manner that the minister guides the head of the patient, and puts his fingers into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth with one of his hands, if the dislocation is on both sides;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two fingers are placed apart, to make even;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften his jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let the mire (mirror or sight) be equal, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if the resetting is difficult, especially when these are the two jaws together, then apply warm oil and oil to them, so that the resetting becomes lighter;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	Nor do we speak of resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset equally, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening, then put on dressings moistened with a mixture made of oil rosat and wax, then tie them lightly with soft bindings;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on their back, and their head be steady between two cushions, so that they do not move either to the right or to the left, nor make an effort to chew, but take light food, until the pains are reduced, and the jaws are numb;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then chew what it wants lightly, and does not labor to open the mouth of the jaw and the drinker, as long as the mandible is well cleaned and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place at one hour, and are not converted to their uses, then come fevers and accustomed sweats, and by chance comes a purging of the belly, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is a sign of a prediction;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times he whom it happens to, dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the force or strength
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The force cannot dislodge what is stuck in the continuity of the chest and the back, and is sometimes dislocated at the thigh, and one can feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on their back, and stretches out their arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the limb firmly with your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on a plaster and bind it, and make it tight;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the joint which is turned towards the hip cannot be dislocated;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does not, and if it dislocates again, reset it to its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put on a plaster and bind it, and make it tight, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healthy;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and likewise the head of the shoulder is reset when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	of what is it that the dislocation occurs at the part of the joint at the elbow
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the part of the wrist
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and by chance it dislocates at the upper part, and that happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and not dislocated behind at the shoulder, and not dislocated inward for the kidneys;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and often dislocates downward toward the joint, especially to those who have little flesh, for to them it is a sudden and hasty movement;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	to those who have sufficient flesh, it happens with effort, and enters with effort.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men a percussion or fracture, and inflames the shoulder with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It is necessary then that you examine it, until you are certain of it;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begins the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that dislocation occurs when it is downward towards the armpit, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a noticeable diversity;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the armpit to the touch the head of the shoulder, as if it were an elbow;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring his hand to his neck, nor move with any movements;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it manifestly at the touch;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this kind of dislocation is not difficult to reduce, when it is recent, or if the sinew is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the ministers raise the hand of the patient up high, then put your fingers below the armpit, and lift the joint with force upwards to its place;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the minister raises the hand, and stretches it up, then puts on a dressing.
si venra hastanment.	if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said in the mornings after, then it is fitting that the patient be bathed in warm water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and let the anointing be soothing and softening, such as a decoction of dock and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be anointed;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then let the patient be laid on their back, and put on a dressing a bandage of equal thickness, not too soft nor too hard, then let the physician place his heel on the bandage, and lift the head of the shoulder gently, and pull the hand of the patient;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another minister holds the head of the patient, so that it does not move downwards;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	That swelling returns now, and if you see it reset in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and have the bone that is larger than the patient's;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and be straight towards the ribcage, and push the shoulder down from the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit up high, so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another attendant pulls the patient's hand downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too lightweight, then hang with him something weighted, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And the resetting is done in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is that you place a stick on the ground, whose thickness is like a pestle, and is neither too large nor too small;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it should be placed under the patient, but so that he has his shoulders draped upwards, and the patient should be standing from the length of the stick;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then his hand should be extended downwards from the other side of the arm, and the joint will return to its place quickly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then make this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take a piece of two arms in length and four fingers in width, which has the head bent back to enter inside near the bottom of the shoulder, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	Then tie a cloth around the head of the fist, so that the fist does not harm the patient, then put it under the armpit of the patient;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend his arm on the fist of the long one, and tie the shoulder to the fist, and the arm to the head of the hand, then put the arm on a stick of a wide chair, and let the hands hang downwards, and let the body hang from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint returns to its place now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever manner that may be, then you must put under the shoulder a layer of even wool, then put the plaster mixed with powdered millet, with incense and absorbent vinegar, on the entire shoulder and around, then strain under the shoulder strongly, and turn the linen on the plaster, and wrap the arm at the neck, and let the hand remain in place.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he moves little, so that the limbs are comforted, for it will heal more quickly;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then move more after 5 or 7 days, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is firm and not loosened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come, or for another reason, then it is necessary that you administer cauterizations to three parts, as it is stated before in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all that, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
