Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is towards the chest, and the breasts, or behind, if made by impulse, and stretching of hands, and one administers another ointment;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cures it until it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing, stiffness comes to the limb, and slowness in movement, then let the patient bathe many times, until that stiffness is alleviated, and it returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the thigh
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	know that the joint of the thigh is dislocated at the hips, and at the hips it returns;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it is dislocated on all sides, and likewise in front and behind, and the dislocation is not responded to, for one sees it well and feels it well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick joint with the sound one, if you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is strained, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it so that the abscesses of the foot are gone, for if the abscesses of the foot came, it would be grievous to reset;
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by chance it cannot be reset from all at once, likewise when it is behind;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	if it is worse than the other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and by chance death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is such that when it can be brought back, you extend your hand with both hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and its arms are stretched out, and the hands are placed according to the joint, above and below, and the joint is pushed towards his chest together, or to the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he doubles his hand on his hand, and strikes from the root of the palm the joint that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer a strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and two ministers hold it, so that it does not move during the extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm from each side, after you have enveloped it in a double cloth that is long and wide;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the mire sets a joint in its articulation, if he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then warms the joint thoroughly, until it recovers;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, put on a dry plaster with some wool or yarn, and warm thoroughly, and bind the arm to the patient's neck, and leave it for some hours, then undo it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage, and let it be;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint does not bind well, restart the plaster and the bandage, and let it be for some hours, until it is firmly set;
puis le deslie.	then undo it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels grit or gravel after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub it thoroughly, and press until it is alleviated;
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	Where you put on the joint a plaster of fat wool, then let it be for a day and a night, then remove it, and make it enter into the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when it sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put the plaster on again, and then enter into the bath;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this two or three times, until it is healthy;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you want, put on a piece of moist cloth warmed with butter, and strain it on;
si revenra a sa disposition.	so that it returns to its condition.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its displacement is slight, more than the other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it is necessary to bring it back to its place quickly, in the same way that it was dislocated, so that the limb is not weakened, or that an abscess does not form.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the treatment is that you put the bad hand on a table, and extend the good hand, and look at the bad hand equally, so that it puts its palm on the surface of the joint, and bends until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	In any case, it is necessary that you check if it is well in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then put the bad hand with the back of its palm on a table for extension and for treatment.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then put the bad hand with its back on the table, and look to put the hand on the same surface of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it's good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then apply a poultice of warm abscesses and let it be without restarting the treatment.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if it cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some hours, the joint remains twisted;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and do not touch the patient's arm unless it is swollen, and they cannot stretch any thing at all:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then you should know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries;
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	if there is no other remedy except to stretch by cauterizing the affected part, and it happens by chance that there is nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the arm is in place, put on the plaster that we have mentioned, then stretch it and leave it for 5 hours, then unbind it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot be well moved, and there is some stiffness, then take a warm cloth, and rub it until it is healthy.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes to the back of the palm or to the front;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then take the fingers and push the dislocation to your pouches as far as it will go, then hold the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is dislocated;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and let it be two hours, and then put it even with that hour;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and anoint the limb, as we have said, and the joint of the hour, and make it move, and anoint it again;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, until it is straight, and also do this, if it is dislocated at the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and also do this, when it is dislocated in another place.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Drop the dislocation of the shoulder bone at the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder bone in the back or neck is dislocated, where there are multiple dislocations, if there is no point of treatment, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the symptoms are that the evacuations come out spontaneously, cannot be held, and many times some members become weakened, either the two hips or the right arm or the left.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often the shoulder moves to four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which moves backwards is called "gilbositez":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	the treatment is that you should rewarm the gilbositez when it comes from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is no point of cure or healing of the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from a fall or blows or similar things, the ancient manners of cure say with great words, but there is not much profit in all of them;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed treatments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling that comes to the chest before, neither injury nor health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes directly to both sides, and one cannot cure the abscesses that come to the back, as I have said;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient should be stretched out on their face in one position, and have a bandage placed under them, so they do not slip;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then fix one stick to the head on the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a string under the shoulders of the patient, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two attendants hold the strings, one to the head and the others to the feet, between the two sticks;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and are well strengthened, the tendons as we have said, and the muscles put their palms on the spine strongly, until it recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not recover with this treatment, take a table three bracles in length, and shave the area around it, and let the patient be on the side, and put the head of the table under the area, then put the middle of the table on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and put the master's feet on the other end of the table, and press firmly, until it recovers to its place;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see that it is done, then make it at the turning which turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you attach two tendons at the head of the patient's arm of a great size, and towards the feet two others, and have between each tendon, above and below, a palm of space in length;
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and it has in each season a piercing, where the thread passes through, and the season is firmly on the ground, so that it does not move;
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between two seasons it has one season that turns, for which the thread turns, and it has in two turnings two small seasons of a palm's length, to turn the thread.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then put the thread that is among the bones at the turning towards the head, and the other thread towards the feet at the other turning, and each of the ministers turns its turner for all the thread, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, then put on a plaster made with a mixture of egg and water, and then the poultices, and then the stake of a tablet three fingers in length, which supports the joint of the hip and the part of the spine, then tie with a thread, as we have said, and use the patient's subtle nourishment, until they are healthy;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if something comes at the end of the sickness, then it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the steel that we have mentioned before;
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and sometimes one must administer a piece of plaster, and sometimes the appearance comes in the posterior spine of the back, and it is thought that this is a dislocation;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone that is exposed, because of which one should not have presumption:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	by chance sudden death comes.
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the thigh
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	It is known that the joints of the thigh and the joints of the shoulder only come out in dislocations, nor do they come out like the other joints;
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the joint of the thigh is dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	downward and upward, and forward and backward;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and further inside the shoulders, and a little dislocated forward and backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the recognition of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the diseased thigh with the sound one, if it is longer, and opens up the patient's knee more than the sound one, and the patient cannot bend their knee to the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and the member that is next to the swollen abscess becomes hot, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who has a fever, it is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of one who has it in front, it is that their thigh is well according to the accomplishment;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	In any case, do not bend the knee without pain, and if you want to make it move, then it cannot before, and retains its urine, and swells the groin, and when one walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of the one who has a dislocation are that he cannot stretch his knee, nor bend it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is out of place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The reminder of this kind of dislocation is that you should consider whether the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its condition, if there is no prompt treatment;
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it does not matter that he has a swelling.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four manners of dislocation, then hasten that you turn the joint, and stretch it from within and without, and move it to the right and left;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	by chance if it returns, and there is no need for another treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then it is necessary that you apply a strong minister, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or with a bandage that is tied above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and one minister extends his hand upwards in a similar manner that he bends his hands downwards towards his shoulders, then tightens with a soft thread on the thigh;
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another ties at the head of the thread;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of stretching is common to four similarities, and if the dislocation has recurred, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If not, then it is necessary to apply a treatment to its similarity.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the shoulder joint, then you must place the patient on his healthy side, then put the thread at the root of the thigh, and the limb which is below the hip, then stretch the thread upwards towards the hip, and towards the strength;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	Then take another minister of his arms, and embrace the large limb of the hip of the patient, and stretch it to the right side firmly:
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	if it returns to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot constrain it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft rope under the two heels, and under the two knees, and let the diseased leg be extended two fingers more than the other;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then let it hang from the head of a pole, and let it be above the ground two arms length;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then command one minister to embrace the head of the hip, and let another minister be hanging with the patient, who firmly embraces the hip, for the joint returns now quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is in the thigh, instruct the patient, as we have said regarding one who has a deformity, and stretch the tendon above the sick thigh properly, and above the foot also;
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two splints, one at the head and the other at the feet, then fix the splint between the groins of the patient in the middle of the form;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and let moist cloths be applied inside, so that they do not bother the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and the surgeons put their hands equally on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put on the table, and press thus as we have said regarding deformity, and instruct the patient to rest on the affected side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the sick thigh immediately, and according to what I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and put his right hand on the patient's shoulder, then press with the other hand, and stretch downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is in the thigh, it is not necessary to stretch the patient downwards, or lift him up from the ground, but rather that he should be as if his hip was dislocated upwards, as we have said about lying on the two hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and let it be on his face, and the leg stretched out as we have said before, and one must press on the joint at the thigh;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be perfect when the patient stretches his legs, and they will be even;
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then join the thighs, and apply a plaster, and bind with a bandage, so that the hip does not move;
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and let it rest for three or four days, then undo it, and put the plaster on again;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are even, then hold them back, as before, and let them be for three days;
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then unbandage it, and make it walk gently, until the limb is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knees are dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inward, outward, and backward;
et ne desalue point devant.	and not dislocating at all to the front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg to his thigh, and if it does not adhere to his thigh, know that it is dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back against his face, and put his foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	Then take your knee in your palms, and pull it between your thighs, then bend the two sides of the knee joint together.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another minister stretches his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that it is well for his leg to be lightly put back on his thigh;
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and put the plaster on, and make the leg adhere to the thigh, and bind them together strongly for three or four days, then undo it;
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and do not exert the patient to go, as long as the limbs are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not in place, then minister strongly as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankles are sometimes sprained, and sometimes completely dislocated, inwardly and outwardly.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the shin is swollen, and it is pulled towards the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the forearm is lightly moved, and the arm is slightly extended by his hands when it is simply massaged.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated from the whole, then you must make the patient sit straight, and hold the ankle firmly from behind the leg, above the shin;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it high, and nicely push the foot upwards;
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot;
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it returns to its place, that's good;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, then resume the work, for it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return in that way, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and fix the ankle firmly to the ground between his thighs, and tie the sheets around, so he does not move the limb;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then let the minister anoint the thigh, and another minister holds the foot in his hands or at his leg, so that he lies on the hill of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then each minister holds equally, and the straps are repeatedly between the thighs of the patient to hold the patient when they stretch it;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then put the minister equally to the dislocation in his hands, and another minister anoints the sound thigh above, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is in place, put the plaster and stop up above, and strengthen firmly, and tie the foot to the thigh, and beware of the nerves which are above the knee behind, that the ligaments are not too tight;
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then let it be for two days or three, and if the ligaments become soft, then strengthen them;
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then untie it on the third or fourth day, and have the patient urinate for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if it goes beyond this limit, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a posthernial abscess comes, then you must treat it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the fingers
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the fingers are dislocated, then you must gently extend them without force, and it is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any of the joints of the foot or toes, then you must have the patient sit on a flat surface or on a table with their leg straight, and put your foot on what opens up the joint, then press firmly with your foot until it returns to place;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is even, and does not open at all, then put between the sole of the foot and a board two sticks, then strain firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it;
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and have it rest, until it is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of a wound and of a dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, often it happens that the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not gentle and merciful and slow, nor harsh;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and apply at the beginning of things that bring about a hot abscess, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you do see hope, then reset the limb in place, so that the hot abscess may come to a head;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, then administer things that bring about a hot abscess, and treat the wound, as it requires, with dried and powdered remedies;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and with the dislocation of a fracture, and the bones are out of joint, if they are fractured, and do what we have said in simple illnesses;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and guard yourself from entering into the way of fear, according to what I have said, for this is of value to you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arm and your body.
